A complex system of arterial anastomoses between the gastroduodenal, splenic (SA) and superior mesenteric artery (SMA) exists. During pancreas transplantation arterial reconstruction between the SA and SMA is performed by using a donor iliac Y-graft. Graft thrombosis is still responsible for up to 10% of graft losses. The aim of this study was to investigate arterial vascularization of the pancreas with special regard to the anastomoses within the pancreatic head. Methods. Ten pancreas grafts considered not suitable for transplantation were removed and a canula was inserted into the splenic artery and the SMA ligated. Results. Angiography showed excellent perfusion of the pancreaticoduodenal arcade via anastomoses in all cases after ex vivo injection of 5 ml of contrast medium into the splenic artery only. All 15 patients analyzed had normal graft function and sufficient perfusion of the pancreatic head. Conclusions. Schlussfolgerungen. Ein ausgedehnteres Resektionsausmaß scheint neben der geringeren operationsspezifischen Morbidität auch zufällig entdeckte Karzinome optimal therapeutisch zu erfassen. Basedow operiert wird. Virtuelle Halsexploration bei Hyperparathyreoidismus und zervikaler Voroperation  Postoperative haemorrhage after thyroidectomya potential lifethreatening complicationaction instead of reactionan algorithm Background. Postoperative haemorrhage is the only potential life-threatening complication after thyroid surgery. Therefore we analyzed our patients for the incidence of postoperative haemorrhage focusing on critical incidences. Methods. We carried out a retrospective study including a standardized protocol to analyze the incidence and the critical events in reoperation for acute postoperative haemorrhage after thyroidectomy focusing on patients with an urgent need of tracheotomy. Results. Out of 26.054 thyroid operations, 428 patients had to undergo reoperation for postoperative haemorrhage (i.e. 1.6%). In 9 of them, tracheal intubation and sufficient oxygenation failed and an acute tracheotomy had to be carried out. We accurately worked up these cases. On the basis of this experience, a standardized procedure for the case of acute airway distress due to acute thyroid haemorrhage has been developed in cooperation with our Department of Anaesthesiology. The guideline includes all steps of clinical procedures, surgical interventions and mod-ern methods and tools for difficult airway management (Bullard-Laryngoscope, GlideScope, Airtrack, Mc Grath). Conclusions. The airway obstruction due to postoperative haemorrhage after thyroidectomy needs a defined concept of all the immediate medical staff in close cooperation with surgeons, anaesthesiologists, ward physicians, nurses and non-medical personnel e.g. hospital orderly, hospital patient transporters and Operating Room assistants etc. A standardized procedure -a defined and trained algorithm -is mandatory and includes the need of interprofessional and interdisciplinary coordination and cooperation. Background. Previous approaches did not result in routinely practicable continuous nerve stimulation methods for the function of the recurrent laryngeal nerve during thyroid surgery. Therefore, we developed a suitable new vagus-nerve electrode. Methods. The vagus-nerve electrode is made of an elastic conductive material. It is specially designed, such that it can be wrapped around the vagus-nerve and 'locked' that way, that it remains in its position throughout the entire operation. The new electrode is characterized by selective contact areas extremely well conducting the stimulation current and adapts to different nerve diameters. A prospective study protocol aimed at a systematic investigation of the new tool. The new Avalanche allows us to analyze the variability of electrophysiological responses. Results. The electrode was used successfully with 54 nerves at risk. The mean delay to apply the electrode around the vagusnerve was 4 min. Repetitive stimulation with 0.5-1.5 mA current provided reliable muscle compound action potentials of the vocal cords. In our data analysis, we will evaluate the different intraoperative continuous electrophysiological responses during thyroid surgery, such as nerve conduction velocity, magnitude of the response or stimulation-threshold for the prediction of imminent recurrent laryngeal nerve injury. Conclusions. The new vagus-nerve electrode allows acquiring reproducible significant muscle compound action potentials as a result of continuous vagus-nerve stimulation. The search for a practical method of permanent intraoperative information of recurrent nerve function to the surgeon may be achieved successfully. The new goal is the early intraoperative warning of an imminent laryngeal recurrent nerve injury. Von der Klinik aufs Land. The interdisciplinary tumour board in a community hospital: the best available tool for quality and safety control for the cancer patient Background. About 70% of all cancer patients, which is the majority, receive most of their cancer care in community hospitals. The tumor board in our community hospital offers a multidisciplinary patient-oriented conference that leads to improved cancer patient care and education of the treating physicians as well. Methods. Multidisciplinary experts dealing with cancer care meet at a weekly schedule. These experts' consensus-decisions are documented by protocol during tumour board runtime and integrated in the hospital provided documentation system (MEDOCS + ). This consensus is elaborated either by using the best recent evidence of treatment option or by presenting the patient to a randomised controlled clinical trial. Results. Between 11=2005 and 11=2007 446 consultations of 402 cases were presented mainly by the surgeon in the weekly tumour board. A mean number of seven patients, which can be handled effectively in one hour, were discussed per board session. Eighty four percent of the patients had a curative oncological treatment concept. Eighteen percent had neoadjuvant treatment and 66% were scheduled for primary operation. Sixteen percent received no treatment or best supportive care. Conclusions. The establishment of a weekly tumour board is easily possible by help of a jour-fixe-schedule. The compositions of the patient cohort as well as all decisions ever made to a particular patient are transparent at all times. This means more treatment safety for the patient and the treating physicians as well. Background. The purpose of this study was to evaluate the midterm results of a new combined surgical and endovascular technique for the treatment of thoracic aortic aneurysms and dissections. Methods. Between August 2005 and December 2007, twelve patients (53.6 AE 14.8 years; 8 male, 4 female) with aortic pathologies (7 dissections, 5 aneurysms) underwent replacement of the ascending aorta and the aortic arch, and simultaneous stent graft implantation into the descending aorta. Size dynamics of the false lumen and aneurysm sac were analyzed on the basis of the maximum dimension of the excluded aneurysmal space and the maximum aortic diameter obtained on computed tomography before hospital discharge and every six months thereafter. Results. The technical success rate was 100%. All patients survived during the follow-up period, but one patient suffered from postoperative stroke. The follow up period ranged from 1 to 18 months. There were no instances of aneurysma sac rupture during the follow-up period. Postoperative computed tomography scans showed complete thrombosis of the aneurysm or dissection within the entire zone of the stentgraft placement. Conclusions. The combined surgical and endovascular technique described in this report proved effective for the treatment of extended aortic lesions. The perigraft space thrombosed completely within the zone of the stentgraft. Background. The aim of the study was to determine late vascular events in patients after endovascular stent-graft placement of thoracic aortic diseases. Methods. From 1996 through 2007 a total of 174 patients (mean age 67a) underwent endovascular stent-graft placement of thoracic aortic diseases at our institution. Indications were aneurysms (n ¼ 87), acute and chronic type B dissections (n ¼ 42), penetrating ulcers (n ¼ 33) and traumatic transsections (n ¼ 12). Results. During a median follow-up of 42 months (1-108 months), in 21% of patients, late vascular events were observed. The highest incidence was observed in patients after stent-graft placement for type B dissections (29%), closely followed by patients after stent-graft placement for penetrating ulcers (24%). The incidence after stent-graft placement for aneurysms was 18%. No events were observed in patients after traumatic transsections. Interestingly, patients undergoing stent-graft placement due to dilatative arteriopathy developed further dilatations in other regions and patients undergoing stent-graft placement due to obliterative arteriopathy were more prone to sustain obliterative diseases in other vascular beds. Conclusions. This study clearly outlines the necessity of a close follow-up in these patients, not only to assess long-term outcome of endovascular stent-graft placement, but also to monitor these patients for new vascular pathologies. A novel approach to the disease mechanism and to the treatment algorithm of intramural hematomas affecting the entire thoracic aorta Background. To reevaluate the disease mechanism and the treatment algorithm of intramural hematomas affecting the entire thoracic aorta. Methods. Within a two-year period, we treated seven patients with this pathology by endovascular stent-graft placement. In all patients a small atherosclerotic plaque at the lateral wall or at the concavity of the aortic arch could be identified as the underlying cause of the disease. One patient required extension of the proximal landing zone by autologous double transposition prior to stent-graft placement. Results. Endovascular stent-graft placement were performed successfully in all patients. By covering the suspected primary lesion, resorption of the intramural hematoma of the entire thoracic aorta could be achieved in all patients. Mean follow-up is 16 months (4-25 months) . Conclusions. By careful diagnostic evaluation, a small atherosclerotic plaque at the lateral wall or at the concavity of the distal aortic arch may be identified as the underlying cause in many cases of intramural hematomas affecting the entire thoracic aorta. Thereby an endovascular approach may be equally effective as conventional ascending and hemiarch replacement. Background. To determine mid-term durability of endovascular stent-graft placement in patients with perforating athero-sclerotic ulcers (PAU) involving the thoracic aorta and to identify risk factors for death as well as early and late cardiovascular events. Methods. From 1997 through 2006, 27 patients (mean age 66 yrs) presented with PAU (rupture n ¼ 7). Mean numeric Euro-SCORE was 11 and mean logistic EuroSCORE was 35. Median follow-up was 42 (10-86) months, being complete in all patients. Outcome variables included death and occurence of early and late cardiovascular events. Results. In-hospital mortality was 11%. Primary success rate was 100%. Actuarial survival rates at 1, 3 and 5 years were 93%, 78% and 70%, respectively. Hemodynamic instability (OR 2.5; p ¼ 0.034) as well as logistic EuroSCORE (OR 2.8; p ¼ 0.019) were identified as independent predictors of early and late cardiovascular events. Conclusions. Endovascular stent-graft placement in patients with PAU is an effective palliation for a life-threatening sign of a severe systemic process. Hemodynamic instability at referral and a high preoperative risk score predict adverse outcome. During mid-term follow-up, patients are mainly limited by sequelae of their underlying disease. Bilirubin suppresses activation of mitogen activated protein kinases associated with ischemia and reperfusion injury Background. Induction of HO-1 has been shown to effectively ameliorate ischemia reperfusion injury (IRI). HO-1 degrades heme into carbon monoxide (CO), free iron and biliverdin. Biliverdin is subsequently converted to bilirubin. Accumulating evidence now suggests that bilirubin may account for the beneficial effects of HO-1. Aim of this study was to determine whether administration of bilirubin has beneficial effects on IRI by measuring mitogen activated protein kinase (MAPK) activation. Methods. Isogenic C57Bl=6 hearts (n ¼ 4=group) were transplanted heterotopically after 18 h of cold ischemia. Bilirubin was administered either by rinsing the graft (125 mM) or i.v. injections to the donor and=or the recipient at 17.5 mg=kg. Grafts were harvested 15 min after reperfusion. Lysates were probed for the total (T) and the phosphorylated (P) forms of ERK 1=2, JNK 1=2 and p38-MAPK. P=T ratio was quantified by ImageJ software and statistically analyzed using ANOVA. Results. Phosphorylation of ERK and p38-MAPK was increased after 18 h of ischemia (prior to reperfusion) when compared to non ischemic hearts. This was not seen in any of the bilirubin treated groups. At 15 min after reperfusion, activation of all MAPKs was observed. At this time point, bilirubin treatment caused a significant inhibition of ERK and JNK (p < 0.001) as well as p38-MAPK (p < 0.05) phosphorylation. Conclusions. Bilirubin treatment inhibits MAPK activation what may account for the protective effects in IRI. Bilirubin treatment may be a promising strategy to improve outcome after solid organ transplantation. Background. Prognosis of ischemic heart failure is poor and therapeutic options are limited. Shock wave therapy (SWT) reportedly induces VEGF overexpression in ischemic skin flaps and ischemic myocardium. Here, we hypothesized that epicardial SWT improves ventricular function by enhancing angiogenesis in an experimental model of ischemic heart failure in rats. Methods. Adult Sprague Dawley rats were subdivided in 3 groups: sham-operated (sham), infarcted myocardium with epicardial SWT (SWT group) and infarcted myocardium without epicardial SWT (control). Four weeks following myocardial infarction (MI), epicardial SWT (100 impulses at 0.15 mJ=m 2 ) was applied directly to the infarcted region in the SWT-group, control animals were untreated. Cardiac function was evaluated using echocardiography before MI, 4 weeks after MI and 12 weeks after SWT. Angiogenesis was evaluated 12 weeks after treatment in serial sections stained with von Willebrand Factor antibody, which were digitalized and morphometried. Results. As compared to sham group (50 AE 4%), left ventricular function decreased in the SWT (21 AE 9%, p < 0.001) and control (18 AE 4%, p < 0.001) group 4 weeks after MI. Fourteen weeks after epicardial SWT, left ventricular function improved in the SWT-group as compared to 4 weeks after MI (37 AE 8%, p ¼ 0.021) and as compared to the controls (21 AE 4%, p < 0.001). Quantitative histology revealed more vital cells (384 AE 84 cells= field in SWT vs 288 AE 56 in controls, p ¼ 0.02) and enhanced angiogenesis (7.1 AE 3.3 vessels=field in SWT vs 3.2 AE 1.8 in controls, p ¼ 0.016) in the SWT group. Conclusions. Direct epicardial shock wave therapy improves left ventricular function and induces neoangiogenesis an experimental model of ischemic heart failure in rats. Epicardial shock wave therapy induces neoangiogenesis and improves left ventricular function after myocardial infarction in pigs in vivo Background. Therapeutic options of ischemic heart failure are limited. Shock wave therapy (SWT) reportedly induces VEGF overexpression in ischemic myocardium. We hypothesized that epicardial SWT improves ventricular function in an experimental model of ischemic heart failure by inducing neoangiogenesis. Methods. Pigs were subdivided in 3 groups: unharmed myocardium with epicardial SWT (healthy control, n ¼ 2), infarcted myocardium with epicardial SWT (SWT-group, n ¼ 6) and infarcted myocardium without epicardial SWT (control, n ¼ 2). Four weeks following myocardial infarction (MI), epicardial SWT (300 impulses at 0.15 mJ=m 2 ) was applied directly to the infarcted area in the healthy control and the SWT-group, controls were left untreated. Cardiac function was evaluated using echocardiography before MI, 4 weeks after MI and 4 weeks after SWT. Angiogenesis was evaluated 4 weeks after treatment by immunohistology with vonWillebrand Factor antibody, which was morphometried with Lucia software. Results. Compared to healthy controls (68 AE 0.7%), left ventricular ejection fraction decreased in the SWT (43 AE 2.5%, p < 0.001) and control group (41 AE 4.2%, p ¼ 0.012) 4 weeks after MI. After epicardial SWT, ejection fraction improved in the SWTgroup as compared to 4 weeks after MI (62 AE 9.1%, p ¼ 0.006), no improvement was observed in the control group (46 AE 5%, p ¼ 0.126). As compared to healthy controls (69 AE 1.4%) ejection fraction normalized in the SWT-group 4 weeks after SWT (p ¼ 0.358), it remained decreased in the control group (p ¼ 0.031). No adverse effects were observed. Conclusions. Epicardial SWT improves left ventricular function after myocardial infarction in pigs. It therefore seems to be an effective and safe therapeutic strategy for the treatment of ischemic heart disease. Does the application of electrical microcurrent heal heart failure by down regulation of the pro-inflammatory cytokines? First pre-clinical in vivo results Unloading of hearts by cardiac assist devices leads to improvement of the hearts function to variable extent. Improvement fails if the extracellular matrix (ECM) shows pronounced remodelling. We investigated the effect of electrical microcurrent (MC) on healing of heart failure with partcular focus of the ECM in in-vivo examinations using spontaniously hypertensive rats (SHR). Two patch electrodes were placed around the hearts of SHR. MC was applied for 5 days. Thereafter, parameter of the ECM of the myocardium was analysed and compared to the myocardium from wild type rats (WKY) and SHR without previous MC application. Gene expression (quantitative PCR) was measured for MMP 2, 3, 8, 9, 13, 14, 16; TIMP 1, 2, 3, 4; connexin 40, 43, 45 and collagen I and III and eventually the level of IL-6. Compared to the myocardium of WKY, the myocardium of SHR without MC application showed a significantly higher level of MMP 3, significant lower level of MMP 8, 14, 16 and an unchanged level of MMP 2 and 13. The TIMPs and connexins were only marginally altered. Collagen I showed an upregulation of 40%. After MC application, MMP 2, 3, 9, 13, 14 and 16 were significantly up-regulated, MMP 8 remained unchanged, and most importantly, collagen I up-regulated by a factor of 2.5. All other analysed parameters were not altered by MC application. The gene expression level of IL-6 was significantly downregulated. MC application regulates MMPs and collagen I on the gene level and normalizes the ECM of hearts in failure. IL-6 was significantly downregulated. MC application initializes a process towards healing of the diseased myocardium. Lipocalin-2, a promising inflammatory marker in acute allograft rejection? Background. Lipocalin-2 (Lcn-2) is associated with ische-mia=reperfusion injury (IRI) in different organs. Data on Lcn-2 expression during allograft rejection have been missing so far. The main focus of this study was to analyze the possible implication of Lcn-2 during acute rejection following solid organ transplantation. Methods. We investigated the expression of Lcn-2 in two different settings: (1) Hearts from male inbred C3H mice were transplanted into C57BL=6 wildtype and Lcn-2 -=recipients. Hearts were recovered at different time points (0 min, 2, 4, 6 and 8d) and Lcn-2 expression was analyzed by conventional histology, Western blot and immunohistochemistry. (2) Serum of 40 patients undergoing orthotopic liver transplantation was collected preoperatively and postoperatively from day 1 to 15. Lcn-2 was analyzed by ELISA and expression levels were correlated with parameters of allograft rejection. Results. (1) Lcn-2 expression already increased in early stages of acute rejection (2d) and significantly correlated with the amount of infiltrating polymorphonuclear cells. Coincidental expression of migration molecules like MIP2 or MMP-9 with Lcn-2 upregulation was observed. (2) Serum levels of NGAL following liver transplantation were elevated 3-7-fold immediately after transplantation due to IRI and also increased prior to clinically apparent acute rejection closely related to elevated laboratory parameters. Conclusions. Our data suggest a chemoattractant function of Lcn-2 in the allograft due to infiltrating immune competent cells. Lcn-2 is an inflammatory marker upregulated during acute graft rejection and its expression prior to clinical parameters of acute rejection might help to identify possible targets for therapeutic intervention. Conclusions. Background. The primary goal of surveillance colonoscopy after resection of colorectal cancer (CRC) is the detection of metachronous neoplasms. The calculated annual incidence for metachronous CRC is 0.35% per year. Identifying patients at risk of developing a metachronous CRC has important implications in their management but remains problematic. Because of greater incidence of microsatellite instability (MSI) in metachronous CRC than in single CRC, MSI might be helpful in predicting the development of metachronous CRC. Methods. This study has examined the value of MSI analysis in identifying patients at risk of developing metachronous cancer after resection of CRC. In 395 patients with stage-III colon cancer participating in a prospective randomized trial microsatellite instability was evaluated using five polymorphic markers. Surveillance colonoscopy was performed every six month for the first five years, and then once a year. The median follow-up time was 84.3 months. Results. Thirty patients had microsatellite instable (MSI) tumors and one of them (1=30; 3.3%) developed a metachronous colorectal cancer six months after primary resection. Microsatellite stable (MSS) tumors were found in 365 patients. 5 patients (5=365; 1.4%) with MSS primary tumors developed a metachronous colorectal cancer (CRC) after a median interval of 44 months. Conclusions. Microsatellite instability does not identify patients at risk of developing a metachronous CRC, although the interval between primary and metachronous CRC seems to be shorter. Several studies have shown, that improved local tumor staging by preoperative MRI leads to a change of surgical management in up to 35% of patients. There is also growing evidence, that the influence of preoperative MRI on surgical therapy can reduce local recurrence rate. In this study we analysed the benefit of preoperative MR-Imaging regarding surgical treatment, local recurrence rate and survival after more than five years of follow up. Methods. The retrospectice study (n ¼ 270) includes all female patients with histologically verified invasive breast carcinoma, which have been operated at our department between 1995 and 2002. Einfluss der Anastomoseninsuffizienz auf die onkologischen Langzeitergebnisse nach Rektumkarzinomresektion Grundlagen. Die Anastomoseninsuffizienz beeinflusst wesentlich die Morbidität und Letalität in der Rektumkarzinomchirurgie. Chirurgisches Management bronchobiliärer Fisteln nach perkutaner Thermofrequenzablation Grundlagen. Sepsis und ihre Folgen sind heutzutage die häufigste Todesursache auf einer Intensivstation. Im Schnitt werden 20%-50% aller Kosten auf einer Intensivstation für die Behandlung der Sepsis aufgewandt. Es ist daher verständlich, dass bei der hohen Letalität und der immensen Kosten, Anstrengungen unternommen werden, die Sepsis frühzeitig zu erkennen, um sie adäquat zu behandeln. Es ist mittlerweile klar, dass die Sepsisbehandlung eine interdisziplinäre Aufgabe für Intensivmediziner, Chirurgen, Radiologen und Mikrobiologen ist. Voraussetzung aber ist es, eine gemeinsame Sprache zu sprechen. Ziel ist es daher, Definitionen und Klassifikationen und ihre Bedeutung für die tägliche Arbeit zu benennen. Definitionen. Eine intraabdominelle Infektion ist eine bakterielle Entzü ndung des viszeralen und parietalen Peritoneums und der angrenzenden Organe. Unter einer Peritonitis hingegen versteht man eine Entzü ndung des Peritoneums, die sowohl bakteriell als auch chemisch sein kann. In der täglichen Praxis aber, wird diese Unterscheidung selten gemacht. Ü blicherweise kann die Erkrankung von einer abakteriellen zu einer bakteriellen fortschreiten. Klassifikation. Die Peritonitis kann auf vielfache Weise eingeteilt werden: nach der Ausbreitung (lokal, diffus), nach dem vorherrschenden Sekret (phänomenologisch -fibrinös, eitrig, kotig, gallig) und nach der Pathogenese (primär, sekundär, tertiär). Chirurgen behandeln hauptsächlich sekundäre Peritonitiden (nach Perforation eines Hohlorganes). Scoring systeme. Die häufigsten Scoring Systeme sind der Mannheimer Peritonitis Index (MPI), der Multiple Organ Dysfunction Score (MODS), der Sepsis related Organ Function Score (SOFA), der Peritonitis Severity Score (PSS) und der Acute Physiology and Chronic Health (APACHE II) Score. Scoring Systeme sind wichtig, um die Prognose des schwerkranken Patienten abzuschätzen. Zusammenfassung. Am häufigsten werden der MPI und der APACHE II Score verwendet, die beide als gleichwertig anzusehen sind, während der Letztere jedoch aufwendiger ist. Chirurgische Therapie und Ergebnisse beim perforierten Ulcus des oberen Gastrointestinaltraktes  A new transoral gastroplasty device for GERD and obesity Background. Gastroesophageal reflux disease and morbid obesity are significant health problems associated with increasing costs. The common surgical therapy is either a laparoscopic or open operation. We are developing a device for endoscopic, fullthickness gastroplasty; the primary goals being reducing the diameter of the gastroesophageal junction (GERD) or the stomach volume (obesity). Methods. The gastroplasty is formed by a new device (Safe-sStitch Medical Inc.) that consists of a flexible tube with an integrated distal excision and suture capsule containing a guillotine excision blade, vertical injection needles and two needles each connected to a suture. A transnasal endoscope is introduced through the device for visualization. Four full-thickness sutures and two mucosal excisions are used for each stage of the gastroplasty. After correct positioning the gastric wall is sucked into the trough and two three-quarter-circle needles rotate 360˚through the captured tissue. To assure the correct cutting depth and haemostasis we inject an adrenaline solution. The second suture-excision-cycle is performed by turning the device and repeating the sequence. The sutures are transoraly tied resulting in a full-thickness muscularis-propria-tomuscularis-propria apposition. Results. We performed pre clinical procedures with ex vivo porcine (n ¼ 45) and human tissue (n ¼ 10) as well as in vivo porcine (n ¼ 5) and canine procedures (n ¼ 5). In each model we were able to create full-thickness gastroplasties. The GEJ circumference changes and the obesity gastroplasty outlet were measured endoscopically. Pre-clinical work has demonstrated the feasibility of the device and its procedures. Two survival canine studies are in progress and will direct further evolution. Grundlagen. Die asymptomatische Trägerin eines in den Choledochus migrierten Titan-Clip nach laparoskopischer Cholecystektomie gab Anlaß Physiopathologie, Therapieoptionen sowie Vermeidungsstrategien dieser Komplikation sowohl der konventionellen als auch der minimal invasiven Chirurgie zu untersuchen. Methodik. 1. case report: Geschildert wird der Fall einer 69jährigen Patientin, die wegen eines Dünndarm-Adhäsionsileus in unserer Abteilung behandelt wurde bei anamnestisch bekannter stattgehabter laparoskopischer Cholecystektomie 15 Jahre zuvor. In der CT-gestützten Diagnostik wurde der asymptomatische intraductale Clip detektiert. In der Folge wurde dieser per ERCP extrahiert. 2. In einer ,,pub-med''-Recherche zu den Schlüsselwörtern ,,clip, migration, choledochus, thread material'' bis zum Jahre 1975 wurde die Literatur zum Thema der Clip-migration und des Kristallisationspotentiales intracholedochaler Fremdkörper, die sich nach GARCIA (1983) in iatrogenen, ingestiven und penetrierenden Ursprunges unterteilen lassen, bezüglich der klinisch relevanten Größen Physiopathologie, Therapieoptionen und Vermeidungsstrategien gesichtet. Ergebnisse. Die Migration von Clips stellt keine spezifische Komplikation der minimal invasiven Chirurgie dar. Aufbauend auf den Beobachtungen und Erfahrungen aus der konventionellen Galle-Chirurgie, insbesondere bezüglich der durch Nahmaterial verschiedenster Qualität gestörten Metastabilität der Galleflüssigkeit, und unter Darstellung weiterer intraduktaler Pathologien des Choledochus werden mögliche physiopathologisch favorisierende Faktoren, die sich aus dem konventionellen oder minimal invasiven Operationsduktus ergeben, erörtert. In der Folge werden Therapienotwendigkeit und -optionen, letztere vor allem im Sinne endoskopischer Prozeduren, auch asymptomatischer intracholedochaler Nidus sowie mögliche intraoperative Vorsichtsmaßnahmen zur Vermeidung des Phänomens der Clip-wanderung besprochen. Schlussfolgerungen. Die Autoren schließen, dass dieses seltene Ereignis im Dekurs kompliziert verlaufender laparoskopischer Cholecystektomien differentialdiagnostisch in Betracht gezogen werden muß und unterstreichen die präponderante Rolle der therapeutischen Endoskopie. Background. Training and certification of aspiring laparoscopic surgeons by use of computed or mechanical simulation and animal models is highly demanded to improve the procedural safety in minimally invasive surgery. A standardized minimal invasive surgery curriculum at the Medical University of Innsbruck (Training Center for Minimally Invasive Surgery) is introduced. Methods. In 12=2007 we implemented a laparoscopic educational program for surgical trainees comprising a three step hands-on workshop: Virtual reality training by use of the haptic version LapSim (Surgicalscience) allows to improve basal technical skills and coordination whereas entire surgical procedures can be mimmicked using a video box trainer (Tübinger Trainer, Wolf). Thirdly, in vivo trocar placement and dissection of vital organs can be trained in an porcine model in the animal lab. Having passed a test on the virtual reality simulator trainees are asked to assist at basic and advanced laparoscopic procedures to become certified. Results. The certification level is defined according to the validated protocols on the virtual reality simulator: Residents start by pointing at balls with the instruments but end up with laparoscopic suturing, clip applying or use of diathermy and ultrasonic instruments. In the wet-lab each trainee has to perform a lap-cholecystectomy and closure of a gastric perforation whereas the laparoscopic team performance is assessed in the animal model demonstrating basic laparoscopic procedures (cholecystectomy, splenectomy, and suturing). Conclusions. The laparoscopic educational curriculum is designed to enable laparoscopic training and skill transfer from virtual reality into the operation room. Grundlagen. Prospektive Analyse von Frühkomplikationen bei minimal invasiver Trichterbrustkorrektur (Nuss-Methode) Background. We report our experiences using the modified minimal invasive method of pectus excavatum repair according to Nuss enriched by thoracoscopic chondrotomy. Patients. Eleven Patients with a mean age of 16.5 AE 2.5 years have been operated using this modification within the last year. Methods. In addition to the Nuss procedure thoracoscopic chondrotomies of the ribs using the lateral incision were performed. The cartilaginous part of the ribs in the area of the funnel was dissected using endoscopic kauterisation. In eight patients an additional oblique wedge shaped partial sternal osteotomy was necessary to reduce physical load and ease the elevation of the sternum. Retrosternal mobilization and introperative stretching of the thorax using a ''rochard-bar'' also modified the operation technique. In three of the eleven patients one Pectus bars with integrated stabiliser plates (PS-Implant + , Fa. Hofer Austria) was implanted, eight patients needed two Pectus bars to minimize the retrosternal pressure. Results. Due to preparation we had one intraoperative bleeding episode of the internal mammaric vessel, one patient developed an extrathoracal haematoma which required surgical intervention. The Vertebral index changed from 34.5 AE 5.9 preoperatively to 23.3 AE 4.3 postoperatively. The cosmetic results in all eleven patients were good to excellent. Conclusions. Thoracoscopic chondrotomies of the ribs even when combined with partial osteotomy of the sternum do not destabilize the chest. Using the described modified extended procedure reduces the retrosternal physical load and makes a postoperative excellent cosmetic result possible also in patients with a deep funnel chest and a stiff thorax. Acute hematogenous osteomyelitis of pelvic bones of children is one of the most difficult to diagnose and insufficiently studied diseases. We analyzed treatment of 18 children with acute hematogenous osteomyelitis (AHO) of pelvic bones treated in the City Children Clinical Hospital and the Regional Children Clinical Hospital during the last 5 years. Among these patients hematogenous way of infection has been found in 11 children, and in 7 -disease developed as the result of injury of pelvic bones. Insufficient knowledge of the clinic of AHO in children is the main cause of errors in the establishment of diagnosis. Diagnosis of AHO of pelvic bones often excluded due to the absence of changes in the roentgenogram of pelvic bones at early stages of the disease. Osteoporosis develops at the 2-3 week of the disease. Periosteal reaction in proliferative phase is manifested non-uniformly. The patchy picture of the bone that noted in this phase, supplemented with the images of the regions of destruction of varying intensity, osteoporosis and sclerosis. Lesion of joints is characterized by dilatation of joint spaces or their narrowing, obscurity of the articular surfaces, osteoporosis, and destruction around articular areas of the bone.Children with suspicion of AHO of pelvic bones must undergo USG, CT and=or MRT of the small pelvis bones and organs, which will permit to establish localization, dimensions of the inflammatory focus in pelvic bones and soft tissues at early stage provide opportunity to control effectiveness of treatment, predict the course and consequences of the disease.  Indoleamine 2,3-dioxygenase and FoxP3 in infiltrating lymphocytes increase with time and severity of rejection in human hand transplantation Background. To better define the characteristics of infiltrating lymphozytes in skin rejection after human hand transplantation, skin biopsies were investigated for expression of FoxP3 and Indoleamine 2,3-dioxygenase (IDO), a key regulatory enzyme to induce T-lymphocyte unresponsiveness. Methods. One hundred and four skin biopsies taken from three bilateral hand transplant recipients during the first 6 years after transplantation were assessed by H & E histology (graded 0-4b) and immunohistochemistry for IDO and FoxP3. Levels of expression were assessed (0; þ; þþ; þ þ þ) and interpreted in the light of clinical courses, time after transplantation, severity of rejection and markers for lymphozyte migration. Results. Rejection ranged between grade 0 and 4a with an average score of 0.94. IDO was found constitutively expressed in the endothelium independent of rejection. IDO expression in the cellular infiltrate was significantly increased upon and correlated well with severity of rejection ( Conclusions. Characteristics of the cellular infiltrate indicate a strong tendency towards self limitation of the alloimmune response towards the skin with both time after transplantation and severity of rejection in human hand transplantation. Background. Matrix Metalloproteinase 9 (MMP-9) is known to be involved in cell migration, tissue repair and remodelling. Lipocalin-2 (NGAL=Lcn-2) forms a complex with MMP-9 preventing it from degradation. Retrieved from previous data about the role of NGAL=Lcn-2 during ischemia and reperfusion (IR) following murine heart transplantation, this study focuses on the interaction between MMP-9 and NGAL=Lcn-2 in analogous settings. Methods. Male inbred C57BL=6 and the Lcn-2 -=mouse were used for heterotopic heart transplantations. RT-PCR, Western blot, gelatine zymography and immunohistochemistry were performed to visualize MMP-9 and NGAL=Lcn-2 expression in the graft at different time points. Polymorphonuclear cells (PMN) isolated from wildtype and Lcn-2 -=mice were used for in vitro experiments. Results. MMP-9 expression was upregulated 8 fold and peaked at 48 h compared to NGAL=Lcn-2 expression which peaked at 24 h. Similar expression patterns were observed in the different experimental settings (Lcn-2 -=donor Lcn-2 -=recipient, wildtype donor and recipient and mixed wildtype=Lcn-2 -=transplantations). However, MMP-9 protein levels were significantly lower in Lcn-2 -=grafts corresponding to a reduced infiltration of PMN in Lcn-2 -=recipients. In vitro PMN retrieved from Lcn-2 -=mice showed lower levels of MMP-9 than from wildtype mice. Stimulation of PMN with recombinant NGAL=Lcn-2 did not increase MMP-9 expression. Conclusions. Our data demonstrate an interaction between MMP-9 and NGAL=Lcn-2 expression during IR in heart transplantation. Reduced MMP-9 expression in Lcn-2 -=grafts is directly related to the simultaneously decreased infiltration of PMN described previously, thus suggesting a chemotactic function of the MMP-9=Lcn-2 complex during IR of the transplanted heart. Bilirubin and biliverdin ditaurate suppress renal ischemia reperfusion injury Background. Heme Oxygenase-1 (HO-1) is crucial in ischemia reperfusion injury (IRI). Biliverdin and bilirubin, products of heme catabolism, at least in part, account for the protective effects mediated by HO-1. We tested conjugated forms of bilirubin and biliverdin in a model of warm renal IRI and a model of kidney transplantation in rats. Methods. Renal arteries of contralaterally nephrectomized Wistar rats were clamped for 45 min. Further, Wistar rat kidneys were transplanted after 18 h of cold ischemia into isogenic recipients. Animals were treated with saline or various doses of bilirubin or biliverdin ditaurate, applied as three i.v. injections covering the perioperative period or a single injection given either before or after reperfusion. Serum total bilirubin was assessed five minutes and serum urea and creatinine was assessed 24 h after reperfusion (n ¼ 4 in each group). Results. An increase in serum total bilirubin before= during reperfusion caused by biliverdin or bilirubin treatment was associated with significantly lower serum creatinine and urea levels at 24 h after reperfusion in the clamp model when compared to the control (p < 0.05). However, when the bile pigments were applied post reperfusion, no effect on kidney function was being observed. In the transplant model, application of biliverdin ditaurate at 30 mg=kg but not at 3 or 10 mg=kg significantly improved kidney function when compared to the control (p < 0.05). Conclusions. Intravenous application of water soluble bilirubin and biliverdin ditaurate prior to reperfusion is feasible and effective in improving kidney function after renal IRI. Tetrahydrobiopterin attenuates renal ischemia reperfusion injury via maintenance of NO homeostasis and stress kinase inhibition Background. Tetrahydrobiopterin (BH4) is an essential cofactor for nitric oxide synthases (NOS) and thus a critical determinant of NO production. BH4 depletion during cold ischemia leads to uncoupling of NOS and contributes to reperfusion injury (IRI) due to increased superoxide formation. The role of BH4 during warm ischemia, however, is still largely unknown. Methods. Ischemic renal injury was induced by clamping the left renal artery for 45 min in male Lewis-rats immediately after right-side nephrectomy. Reperfusion was studied at R0 (no reperfusion), 15 min (R1), 2 h (R2) and 7 days (R3). Animals received either BH4 (20 mg=kg=BW) prior to reperfusion (Group I) or saline (Group II). Sham operated animals served as controls. Renal function was determined by plasma creatinine= urea. BH4 tissue levels were assessed by HPLC. Morphologic changes were quantified by H & E histology. Peroxynitrite formation was assessed by nitrotyrosine-immunostaining and stress kinase (p38, JNK) activation was analysed using phosphorylation specific antibodies. Results. BH4-tissue-levels were slightly increased after 45 min warm ischemia (1.0-1.6 fold) up to two days (R1, R2) when compared to non-ischemic controls. Additional BH4 treatment prior to ischemia significantly improved renal function at all time points studied following reperfusion (all p < 0.001). Furthermore, BH4 reduced ischemia induced histologic damage (increased inflammation, interstitial edema, hemorrhage, tubular atrophy and focal areas of necrosis) and diminished peroxynitrite formation and hence nitrotyrosine staining (R1-R3). Subsequently, stress kinase activation was abrogated following BH4 treatment further limiting ischemia reperfusion injury (p < 0.01). Conclusions. BH4 treatment significantly improves post-ischemic renal function as well as histologic damage and might be a promising novel therapeutic strategy in attenuating IRI via maintenance of NO homeostasis and stress kinase inhibition in kidney transplantation. Prevention of kidney ischemia-reperfusion (I=R)-associated injury: role of mitogen activated protein kinases Background. Ischemia (I) and reperfusion (R) trigger a series of events which culminate in severe injuries to the affected tissue in organ transplantation. Cell death, metabolic alterations and inflammation result in impairment of short-and long term function. Cells respond to extra cellular signals by transmitting intracellular instructions to coordinate appropriate responses. The group of mitogen activated protein kinases (MAPKs) was implicated through aberrant activation in many settings includingI= R-associated organ damage. Although MAPKs are known as critical proteins in cell signaling their role during I=R is controversially discussed. Methods. To asses intracellular signaling and kidney function a rat ischemia reperfusion model was used. Ischemic renal injury was induced by clamping the left renal artery for 45 min in male Wistar-rats immediately after right-side nephrectomy. Reperfusion was studied at R0 (no reperfusion), 15 min (R1), 2 h (R2) and 7 days (R3). Sham-operated animals served as controls. Renal function was determined by plasma creatinine=urea. MAPKs (ERK, JNK, p38) activation was analysed using phosphorylation specific antibodies. Results. In summary, reoxygenation was characterized by a dramatic increase in the activity of ERK (p < 0.05, JNK (p < 0.05) and p38 (p < 0.0001) during early reperfusion. This was associated with a significant raise in creatinine and urea. Data suggest that the use of small molecular weight p38-MAPK inhibitors (SB203580 and SB239063) have a beneficial effect on the ischemia reperfusion injury, showing a decrease in creatinine and urea as assessed 24 h after reperfusion. Conclusions. Renal I=R injury is associated with a significant increase in MAPK activity. Isolated p38MAPK inhibition during ischemia improves kidney function suggesting that p38 may provide a promising target for ameliorating reperfusion injury. NOS cofactor activity is essential for BH 4 associated attenuation of ischemia reperfusion injury following murine pancreas transplantation Tetrahydrobiopterin (BH 4 ) is not only an essential cofactor for nitric oxide synthases but also a strong antioxidant. This study compared the protective effect of BH 4 supplementation previous to organ retrieval with supplementation of 4-amino-tetrahydrobiopterin (ABH 4 ), a pteridin analogue with similar chemical redox behaviour but no cofactor activity. Syngeneic C57BL6 mice were used as size-matched donorrecipient pairs. Cervical heterotopic vascularized pancreas transplantation was performed with a modified no-touch technique. Grafts were subjected to 16 h cold ischemia time (CIT) and different treatment regiments: untreated (I), BH 4 50 mg=kg i.m. (II) and ABH 4 50 mg=kg i.m. (III) both prior to organ retrieval. Non-transplanted animals served as controls (IV). After 2 h of reperfusion intravital fluorescence microscopy was used for analysis of graft microcirculation by means of functional capillary density (FCD). Parenchymal damage was quantified by histology (H&E) and by nitrotyrosine-immunostaining. Following prolonged CIT only pancreatic grafts treated with BH 4 (II) displayed markedly higher values of FCD (I) (p < 0.01). In contrast, pre-treatment of donor animals with ABH 4 (III) did not improve FCD levels. Nevertheless, parenchymal damage as well as peroxynitrite formation were significantly attenuated in grafts of both treatment regiments (p < 0.05). However, acinar haemorrhage and fat necrosis as well as peroxynitrite formation were significantly reduced by BH 4 treatment compared to ABH 4 (p < 0.05). The protective effect of BH 4 supplementation prior to organ retrieval relies on its NOS cofactor activity rather than on its antioxidative capacity. BH 4 might therefore be a novel promising agent to attenuate IRI in clinical solid organ transplantation. Tetrahydrobiopterin supplementation prior to organ retrieval attenuates early parenchymal damage following murine pancreas transplantation Tetrahydrobiopterin (BH 4 ) is an essential cofactor for nitric oxide synthases and a critical determinant of NO production. BH 4 depletion contributes to ischemia reperfusion injury (IRI) after pancreas transplantation. Here we studied the therapeutic potential of donor BH 4 supplementation compared to recipient BH 4 treatment prior to reperfusion. C57BL6 mice were used as size-matched donor-recipient pairs. Cervical heterotopic pancreas transplantation was performed with a modified no-touch technique. Grafts were subjected to 16 h cold ischemia time (CIT) and different treatment regiments: untreated (I), BH 4 50 mg=kg i.m. prior to organ reperfusion (II) and BH 4 50 mg=kg i.m. before organ retrieval (III). Non-transplanted animals served as controls (IV). 2 h after reperfusion intravital fluorescence microscopy was used for analysis of graft microcirculation by means of functional capillary density (FCD). Quantitative assessment of parenchymal damage was done by histology (H&E) and nitrotyrosine-immunostaining. BH 4 tissue levels were measured by HPLC. Following prolonged CIT pancreatic grafts treated with BH 4 either before reperfusion (II) as well as prior to organ retrieval (III) displayed significantly higher values of FCD compared to non treated animals (I) (p < 0.01). BH 4 tissue levels were substantially increased in both BH 4 treated groups. Furthermore, parenchymal damage as well as peroxynitrite formation were significantly attenuated in both treatment regiments (p < 0.05). However, comparing groups II and III, donor pre-treatment showed significantly improved graft microcirculation and morphology compared to recipient supplementation prior to reperfusion (all p < 0.01). Donor pre-treatment with BH 4 consistently reduces post-ischemic deterioration of the graft and might therefore be a promising novel strategy in attenuating IRI in pancreas transplantation. Neuroendokrine Tumore sind seltene Erkrankungen des Magens, bei denen eine weniger radikale chirurgische Therapie oder eine endoskopische Therapie akzeptiert ist. Tumore bis 1 cm Größe bei gleichzeitig vorliegender Typ-A-Gastritis, MEN I oder Zollinger-Ellison-Syndrom werden endoskopisch abgetragen. Größere Tumore oder Tumore mit Infiltration der Lamina muscularis propria werden durch eine Magenteilresektion behandelt. Methodik. Anhand eines aktuellen Falles und der Darstellung der Literatur wird die aktuelle Diagnostik-und Therapieempfehlung hinterfragt. Ergebnisse. Bei unserer Patientin zeigte sich ein gemischtes exokrin-endokrines Karzinom, welches bei Einhalten der gültigen Empfehlungen für Diagnostik und Therapie nicht komplett entfernt worden wäre. Erst die Ausweitung der Therapie um eine Lymphadenektomie hat zur R0-Resektion geführt. Die Literatur zeigt ein uneinheitliches Bild. Schlussfolgerungen. An Hand eines Fallberichtes und der Literatur werden die bisherige Therapieempfehlung kritisch hinterfragt und eine radikale chirurgische Therapie bei allen Karzinoiden über 1 cm Größe und bei neuroendokrinen Karzinomen gefordert. Die alleinige Magenteilresektion birgt die Gefahr des Residualtumors. Immunhistochemischer Vergleich von Chromogranin A, B und Secretoneurin in neuroendokrinen Tumoren Background. The removal of the tumour and of all affected lymph nodes is the treatment of choice in NET cancer. In NET of the small bowel, the extent of intestinal resection is determined by number and distribution of metastasized nodes. So it is mandatory to remove as much of the mesentery as necessary, but as little as possible. Methods. The 52 years old patient presented with small bowel obstruction due to repeated previous abdominal surgery. We removed a bulk of 50 cm of ileum with the signs of chronic adhesive peritonitis. Pathology incidentally identified a so far unknown T3-neuroendocrine carcinoma and six positive nodes. 18FDG-PET then revealed 2 residual lesions in the mesentery, so that we decided to re-operate on the patient. 10 days before her second surgery she had an 111In-Octreotide +scan that confirmed the PET-results. During laparotomy we performed a thorough exploration of the mesentery with a hand-held gamma-detector (C-Trak + ). The probe identified four additional nodes the involvement of which was proven by frozen section. The margins after the resection that we then performed were all clear. Results. Re-stagings three and nine months after surgery including PET, Chromogranine A, and 5-HIA were negative for residual or recurrent disease, and the patient is perfectly well. Conclusions. The intra-operative use of a gamma-probe for 111In-Octreotide + may allow for stage-adjusted surgery in NET of the small bowel. Controversial items in the treatment of neuroendocrine liver metastases H. Cerwenka Background. Due to the rarity and heterogeneity of the disease, some questions on treatment of neuroendocrine liver metastases remain difficult to answer. Methods. Six controversial items are discussed using the most recent literature, published guidelines and own experience. Results. 1) Is it profitable to remove neuroendocrine liver metastases when the primary tumor cannot be completely removed? Yes, if 80-90% of the total tumor load can be resected (debulking). 2) Is it profitable to remove neuroendocrine liver metastases if they cannot be resected completely? The answer is similar to the first one. 3) Is a synchronous resection of primary tumor and liver metastases profitable? Yes, if the overall extent of the operations is tolerable for the patient, if not a two stage procedure with intermittent medical therapy is preferable. 4) Can detection of all lesions be improved by additional imaging techniques? In addition to somatostatin receptor scintigraphy and CT=MRI, special PET techniques and recently developed ''theragnostics'' may be useful. Moreover, intraoprative ultrasonography remains an indispensable surgical tool. 5) Is radiofrequency ablation profitable for unresectable liver metastases? Data are not yet sufficient, but promising. 6) Is liver transplantation an option? Yes, but only for highly selected patients with favorable tumor biology. Conclusions. Due to the variety in biological behaviour, some conventional treatment strategies must be seen differently in patients with neuroendocrine liver metastases. Generally valid rules must be carefully adapted to every single patient providing tailored treatment and interdisciplinary approach. Background. The main indication for microvascular reconstruction of the face is the best possible functional and aesthetic outcome. In several cases of reconstruction of the alveolar ridges of the mandible or maxilla extraoral scars might have been avoided, if microvascular anastomoses may have been performed without extraoral approach. Methods. In six patients with severe defects of the alveolar ridge of the mandible or maxilla caused by trauma or atrophy reconstruction was performed with the use of microvascular bone flaps. Here 3 microvascular corticocancellous femur flaps, 2 iliac crest flaps and one osteoperiosteal fibula flap was used. In every case only an intraoral approach was used for preparation of the transplant bed and the facial vessels. The transplants were fixed to the defect side by miniplate and miniscrew osteosyntheses. The anastomoses were carried out via intraoral approach between the donor vessels and one branch of the facial artery and vein or the main artery and vein themselves. The patients were followed up radiologically and clinically for 6-24 months postoperatively. Results. There was no flap loss or severe complication postoperatively. All patients had good functional and aesthetic results and have been treated successfully with implants 4 to 6 months after microvascular reconstruction. Five of six patients have already been treated with implant retained prostheses. Conclusions. Intraoral anastomosing of microvascular bone flaps is a reliable technique for microvascular reconstruction of the alveolar ridge with severe defects not caused by tumour diseases. Here extraoral scars may be avoided. Ergebnisse. Mandibular midline distraction utilizing a toothborne appliancea consecutive study O. Ploder, R. Koehnke Background. Methods. Twenty patients with transverse deficiencies of the lower arch were treated in this study. Prior to surgical intervention, a custom made appliance was cemented to the teeth and additionally fixed with two screws between the teeth on each side. Distraction was started after five days with 0.6 mm per day. After a retention period of 60 days, the appliance was removed and a retainer was used. Fistula-in-ano denotes the chronic phase of anorectal sepsis and is characterized by chronic purulent drainage and=or the presence of an epithelialized track. The categorization of a fistula-in-ano is dependent on its anatomical location relative to the anal sphincter muscles and the pelvic diaphragm according to Parks classification: intersphincteric, transsphincteric, suprasphincteric, or extrasphincteric. Complex fistulas comprise recto-=anogenital tracks in women, Crohn or recurrent fistulas or involve between 30 and 50% of the external sphincter muscle mass and their treatment is more likely to be associated with a higher risk for impairment of continence. Recent imaging techniques of the pelvic floor (dynamic and conventional magnetic resonance imaging, 3-D reconstruction of CT slices, endoanal and endorectal ultrasound) and plastination histology methods for processing pelvic floor specimens crucially support the pelvic floor surgeon to largely clarify the disposition of the muscular (anal sphincter complex, pelvic diaphragm) and the neurovascular components of the pelvic floor. The anatomical borders, which are already visible in early fetal stages, therefore serve as landmark structures during continence and potency-preserving fistulotomies and fistulectomies. Failed restrictive bariatric procedureconversion or revision: a prospective long term follow-up study Background. Vertcal Banded Gastroplasty (VBG) and later Adjustable Gastric Banding (AGB) were the standard procedures in restrictive bariatric surgery over decades. Conversion to a roux-en-Y gastric bypass (RYGB) has been advocated after the failure of restrictive procedures. The aim of this study was to assess the effect of laparoscopic treatment of complications linked to VBG and AGB with a focus on Revision (AGB) or Conversion to RYGB. Methods. In a prospective study the outcome of patients with a Laparoscopic reoperation after VBG and AGB were analyzed. Patients with a B.A.R.O.S. score (Bariatric Analysis and Reporting Outcome System) over 1 point were considered for an AGB less than one point considered for a RYGB and included into the study. score over 1 and 46 with a score <1. All reoperations were planed laparoscopically. Fourty five patients (20.7%) had multiple laparotomies. We had one conversion to open surgery. In two patients an AGB procedure was not feasible and abandoned due to adhesions and abscess in an eroded banded gastroplasty. We noted 6 perioperative (3.7%) non fatal complications (1 pulmonary embolism, 1 esophagogastric and 1 gastric perforation with intraoperative repair, 2 pneumonia, 1 biliary peritonitis with band removal and 1 trocar wound bleeding). No perioperative or postoperative mortality was noted. In the converted AGB group two complication reoperations (1.1%) were converted to open surgery (biliary peritonitis and postoperative abcess formation after AGB) and none in the RYGB group where no anastomotic leak was observed with no statistical difference in complications between AGB and RYGB, respectively. The hospital stay was 4.2 AE 1.3=range 2-10 days for AGB and 8.4 AE 0.9 days (p < 0.001). The mean follow-up was 63 þ 1 À 44.5 months (6-76 months) with a current follow up rate of 96%. The mean BMI at follow-up was 30.6 AE 5.1 (63% EWL from initial weight) for AGB and 29.6 AE 5.1 (68% EWL from initial weight) for RYGB, respectively. Conclusions. The treatment of complications after VBG with an AGB and RYGB is safe and effective. Failed VBG and AGB with an initial good to excellent BAROS result should be considered again for a restrictive procedure, namely the adjustable gastric banding procedure with a shorter operating time and hospital stay. The international consensus summit for sleeve gastrectomy in New York 2007 Over the last 15 years, obesity surgery has developed tremendously. The two most frequently laparoscopically performed procedures are the adjustable gastric banding and the gastric bypass. A new intervention has recently appeared: the sleeve gastrectomy, an essentially restrictive intervention consisting of a vertical gastrectomy including the entire greater curvature of the stomach while leaving in place an approximately 100-ml gastric tube along the lesser curvature. Sleeve gastrectomy (SG) was initially added as a modification to the biliopancreatic diversion (BPD) and then combined with a duodenal switch (DS) in 1988. It was first performed laparoscopically in 1999 as part of a DS and subsequently done alone as a staged procedure in 2000. With the revelation that patients experienced weight loss after SG, interest in using this procedure as a bridge to more definitive surgical treatment has risen. Benefits of SG include the low rate of complications, the avoidance of foreign material, the maintenance of normal gastro-intestinal continuity, the absence of malabsorption and the ability to convert to multiple other operations. Reduction of the ghrelin-producing stomach mass may account for its superiority to other gastric restrictive procedures. SG should be in the armamentarium of all bariatric surgeons. Nonetheless, long-term studies are necessary to see if it is a durable procedure in the treatment of morbid obesity. Especially in orofacial surgery anatomic form, function and esthetics present an inseparable unit with any deflection in reconstructive and esthetic surgery resulting only in camouflage of the respective disease. For this reason the society for implantology and tissueintegrated prosthesis (GIGIP) has endorsed evidence-based surgery for the face under the guidelines ''form and esthetics follows function'' since its foundation in 2003. The management of maxillofacial defects has rapidly changed in the last decade. Functional and aesthetic requirements have steadily increased along with the refinements of microsurgery. Patients after ablative tumor surgery or who survive noma e. g. develop a mutilated and disabled face. The sequelae include extensive midface defects and oral incompetence (Swartz et al. 1986 , Montandon 1991 , 2007 , Hidalgo et al. 1994 , Igawa et al. 1998 , Cordeiro et al. 1999 , Baratti-Mayer et al. 2003 . Intense scarring leads to disfigurement and restriction of jaw movement esp. in noma. The fact that the basis for important functional aspects like speaking, mastication, deglutition and effortless respiration are localized in the maxillofacial area, dictates the goal for any treatment: The most lifelike restoration possible. To match these requirements microsurgery has entered its third generation by the new principle of the prefabricated composite grafts. The distraction osteogenesis is now simultaneously being established as a treatment modality of first choice. To date the most frequently used technique for reconstruction of extended defects is the transfer of vascularised osseous respectively osseo(-myo-)cutaneous free flaps. (Schustermann et al. 1994 , Wei et al. 1994 , Hayter et al. 1996 , Urken et al. 1998 , Cordeiro et al. 1999 , Wei et al. 2002 Fibula, scapula and iliac crest were the preferred donor sites (Swartz et al. 1986 , David et al. 1988 , Thoma et al. 1991 , Forrest et al. 1992 , Hidalgo et al. 1994 , Nakayama et al. 1994 , Reychler et al. 1994 , Bähr 1996 , Igawa et al. 1998 , Kazaoka et al. 1999 , Shpitzer et al. 1999 , Deschler et al. 2000 . At the beginning attempts were made to prefabricate single separate flap components like the vascular bundle for lengthening purposes (Kärcher 1991). The current project of this nature is the prefabrication of a ''Custom Vascularised Bone Graft in Man'' by dint of ''tissue engeneering'' (Warnke et al. 2004) . First attempts to provide an intracavitary lining in the head and neck region were introduced since the mid-nineties. (Rath et al. 1997 , Chen et al. 1999 , Pribaz et al. 1999 , Delaere et al. 2001 , Jaquet et al. 2004 ). Yet since the evaluation of the aspired clinical results' quality initially oftentimes fell short, a series of new surgical concepts were not able to prevail. Prefabricated complex composite grafts for a complete stateof-the-art reconstruction consist of preformed bone, implants and new mucosa like coverage tightly adherent to the bone and the periimplant region. (Vinzenz et al. 1996 , Holle et al. 1996 , Vinzenz et al. 1997 , Vinzenz et al. 1998 , Igawa et al. 1998 , Rohner et al. 2000 , Rohner et al. 2003 . Up until now the best clinical results could be achieved with this method. Furthermore they are histological and immunhistological evidence based. (Schlenz et al. 2001 , Kunstfeld et al. 2001 ). An alternative approach for the predefined complete reconstruction is the craniofacial distraction osteogenesis. (Mc. Carthy et al. 1992 , Costantino et al. 1990 , 1993 , Samchukov et al. 2001 , Klein et al. 2001 , Odo et al. 2001 , Papageorge et al. 1999 , Polley et al. 1997 , Rachmiel et al. 1999 , Razdolsky et al. 2001 , Guerrero et al. 2001 . By use of a bone transport technique including the distraction histogenesis of the facial tissues and overlying masticatory keratinized gingiva similar results can be achieved -yet with far less effort in surgical setting and aftercare. This reduces risks, costs and enables this technique to be used even in developed countries. Effects of assisting maneuvers on robotic suturing of experimental coronary anastomoses in a beating heart model Background. Robotic endoscopic CABG is mostly performed as solo surgery. We aimed to investigate whether manual assistance can reduce suturing times and enhance the anastomotic suturing technique in TECAB. Methods. In isolated pig hearts the right coronary artery was excised pedicle-like (resembling the IMA) and sutured to the LAD using the daVinci TM telemanipulation system. 7=0 Pronova was used to perform the anastomosis in running fashion. The heart was kept in pulsatile motion by an intraaortic counterpulsation device placed in the left ventricle at 80 bpm. In group I (n ¼ 15) the suture was carried out by the console surgeons (n ¼ 3) in a solo version, in group II (n ¼ 15) the anastomosis was assisted with an endo-forceps. Results. One assisted anastomosis was not completed because of technical difficulties. The anastomosis time was 20.1 AE 5.1 min in assisted vs. 19.0 AE 3.5 min in non assisted cases (p ¼ ns). The comfort level on a scale from 1 to 10 was higher in assisted procedures (7.7 AE 1.8 vs. 6.4 AE 1.9, p ¼ 0.05). There was no difference regarding time for placement of silastic tapes or the intracoronary shunt (p ¼ ns). Suturing problems occurred in 6=15(40%) of assisted anastomosis and in 7=15 (47%) of nonassisted anastomoses (p ¼ ns). All anastomoses were patent on inspection and by probing in both groups. Conclusions. In a wet lab model of robotic coronary anastomoses assisting maneuvers do not decrease suturing speed and occurrence of technical challenges. Similar suturing quality can be achieved if the suture is carried out in solo fashion or assisted. Suturing comfort, however, seems to be higher in assisted procedures. Background. Cardiopulmonary Bypass is known to affect cytokine release, leading to a generalized endogenous immune reaction similar to that of sepsis (Intensive Care Med 2004; 30: 1468 -1473 . In this study we investigated the role of SLPI in ischemia=reperfusion injury and cardiac transplantation. Methods. SLPI-=-mouse hearts and WT controls were transplanted immediately or after 10 h of cold ischemia (CI). Recombinant SLPI (rSLPI) was added to the preservation solution or given systemically. Methods. Background. Endoscopic mucosal resection (EMR) is a commonly used therapeutic procedure for Barrett's esophagus. We have developed a new technique for EMR that utilizes a cold blade. The absence of cautery allows an exact histological analysis of the resection margins. Methods. The mucosal resection technique used was based on a new flexible device (SafeStitch Medical Inc.). The instrument consists of a flexible tube with an integrated distal excision capsule. A transnasal endoscope is introduced into the device for visual orientation. A guillotine blade resects the mucosa. After visual endoscopic identification of the metaplastic area suction pulls the mucosa into the capsule. To assure the correct cutting depth and haemostasis we inject an adrenaline solution. Mucosal excision is performed with a single proximal-to-distal pushing movement of the blade. After removing the device from the esophagus the specimen can be easily orientated for the pathologist. The device was studied for completeness of mucosal resection, uniformity of depth, and safety characteristics of the procedure. Results. A total of 10 excisions were performed on ex-vivo fresh cadaveric human esophagi. The specimens average size was 2.75 Â 2.35 cm. Ninety-eight percent of 150 areas examined microscopically included the muscularis mucosa. In some excisions deep submucosal gland units were present. The average depth of submucosa excised was 0.297 mm. Conclusions. This new device demonstrated reliability and reproducibility of satisfactory excision depth for use in mucosal resection for Barrett's esophagus. Further preclinical study is underway to refine the device for clinical application and study. Background. EMR is increasingly propagated as ''curative treatment'' for early esophageal carcinomas. However, this approach is severely violating oncologic principles and adressing it as ''curative'' seems inappropriate. Methods. A literature review was performed and ten major reasons were identified which clearly indicate the inappropriateness of EMR, when the therapeutic aim is cure. Results. 1) In the majority of cases, EMR can only be performed as 'piecemeal-technique', with removal of the tumor in several pieces. 2) Only in the vast minority of cases a complete ('R0') resection can be achieved with EMR. It is furthermore questionable if it is even justified to apply this R-classification to the fragemented EMR specimen. 3) Early esophageal carcinomas may be associated with lymph node invovement, depending on depth of invasion. 4) It is impossible to accurately define depth of invasion prior to EMR. 5) Esophageal neoplasms do frequently have a multifocal growth pattern. 6) The precancerous mucosa (Barrett's esophagus) remains within the patient. EMR is ''. . .similar to pulling weeds out of a garden and expecting them never to grow again''. 7) Persistence of the underlying etiology: The gastroesophageal reflux is not prevented by means of EMR. 8) Severe impairment of quality of life: Life-long follow-up endoscopies are mandatory. 9) Psychooncologic inadequacy: Patients have to live with the unresolved oncologic problem and the certainty that treatment was not curative 10) Adequate survival data are missing. Conclusions. EMR for early esophageal adenocarcinoma is not a curative treatment. Addressing it in this way should be strongly discourraged. Background. The adequate management of patients suffering from esophageal perforation still remains a therapeutic challenge emphasized by different treatment options reported in literature. The aim of this retrospective study was to review indications, morbidity and mortality of esophagectomy as compared to less aggressive treatment methods. Methods. The study was performed on the basis of a clinical review of 62 patients suffering from esophageal disruption treated at one centre of general thoracic surgery between 1990 and 2006. Results. Esophagectomy was performed in 32 patients, 23 patients were treated with primary repair and 7 patients got conservative treatment as well as endoscopic stent implantation. Sepsis as a main parameter in the treatment algorithm was diagnosed in 36 patients and 32 of 36 patients were treated with esophagectomy with a mortality rate of 18.75%. Mortality rate in the group treated with less aggressive methods was 3.33%. The overall mortality was 11.29%. Conclusions. The policy of primary repair should be adopt whenever possible in patients with no intrinsic esophageal disease and no sepsis. However, the more critically ill the patient, the stronger the argument for esophageal resection. This approach may be the only chance to terminate continued mediastinitis, pleural contamination and loss of saliva and gastric juice through the fistula in order to offer a better chance of survival. Based on our results, the impact and limits of the method are presented. Methods. In the past 3 years, 24 patients (between 56 up to 92 Years of age) with manifestation of the bowel occlusion have been intended for an implantation of a self expanding metallic stent (SEMS). In patients with colonic obstruction, one denied stenting, in next foud did not succeeded to pass the stenosis with guide wire. Implantation of SEMS in our patient collective has been successful only in 66%. The method is safe and effective, when the guide wire passed the stenosis. Surgical management of perforated sigmadiverticulitis with fecal peritonitis using abdominal VAC + to reduce rate of colostomy A. Perathoner, H. Weiss, D. Öfner, R. Margreiter, R. Kafka-Ritsch Background. The standard surgical management of acute perforated diverticulitis with fecal peritonitis is still the Hartmann procedure. We present a new concept of treatment of perforated diverticulitis using abdominal VAC therapy to reduce the rate of colostomy and improve morbidity and mortality of acute complicated diverticulitis. Methods. Between November 2006 and September 2007 30 patients underwent emergency laparotomy at our department for acute perforation of the colon. Eleven patients with perforated diverticulitis and fecal peritonitis (Hinchey IV) were included in this prospective study. Surgical treatment consisted of extensive peritoneal lavage, resection of the perforated colonic segment and application of abdominal VAC therapy to reach rapid clearence of the peritoneal cavity. A colostomy was performed only in patients with deterioration despite VAC therapy, preoperative incontinence or bedridden persons in permanent need of nursing. Results. The median age of patients was 72 years (range 55-81). Five patients ended with a terminal colostomy, two of them died due to severe sepsis with multiorgan failure. The length of abdomial VAC therapy varied between one and six days (median 3 days) with two or more VAC changes in six patients. Three patients developed a superficial wound infection. The median length of hospital stay was 17 days (7 days intensive care unit). Conclusions. The abdominal VAC therapy is a simple procedure, that facilitates a rapid clearence of the abdominal cavity with a high rate of primary anastomosis, acceptable morbidity and fast recovery of patients with fecal peritonits due to perforated sigmadiverticulitis. was to assess whether endoscopically assisted GSV stripping is comparable both surgically and regarding patient quality of life with the standard surgical technique of crossectomy and stripping. Methods. Consecutive patients with primary GSV varicosis were randomly assigned to the two described methods. Combined endpoints of the study were haematoma at the thigh, ecchymosis, seroma, wound healing complications, infections and the change of score for the SF-36 quality of life assessment during follow up at one and four weeks postoperatively. Results. Sixty consecutive patients were enrolled in the study and randomized to endoscopic (n ¼ 30) and to traditional (n ¼ 30) stripping. The combined rate of postoperative morbidity was 32 events (53%), 13 (42%) events in the endoscopic and 19 (63%) in the conventional group (not significant). Regarding the SF-36, patients in the endoscopic group had significantly less pain (p ¼ 0.03). At four weeks, patients in the endoscopic group had significantly less pain (p < 0.005), better physical function (p < 0.005) and physical role (p ¼ 0.01). Conclusions. In this pilot study, endoscopically assisted stripping of the GSV has superior results compared to traditional stripping regarding postoperative quality of life in a randomized population. This method has the potential for general surgeons to compete with endovenous varicose vein therapies. Thyroid surgery can be followed by 3 typical complications i.e. recurrent laryngeal nerve injury, postoperative hypoparathyreoidism and haemorrhage, which can delay discharge from the hospital. Can we perform 24 h surgery for economic reasons? Methods. We carried out a quality-control study to analyze the critical events after thyroidectomy focusing on arguments against early discharge. For the early prediction of hypoparathyreoidism, a prospective study was performed; for the risk of recurrent nerve injury and postoperative haemorrhage, data from large retrospective studies of our patients were analyzed. Results. Long term hypocalcaemia can be excluded on the first postoperative day, when calcium level is 2.2 mmol=l or more (60% i.e. 489=819 of patients undergoing thyreoidectomy). Bilateral nerve injury is a very rare complication (0.1% in benign thyroid disease i.e. 5=4330) and can be verified on the first postoperative day. Out of 26,054 thyroid operations 428 patients had to undergo reoperation for postoperative haemorrhage (i.e. 1.6%), 8 of them with the first sign more than 24 h after the operation (from 25 to 35 h). 1 patient was reoperated after 64 h due to unclear respiratory distress to exclude haemorrhage with slow onset. In addition, the cost-effectiveness of the reduced hospital stay will be evaluated. Conclusions. Safe discharge after thyreoidectomy is possible 36 h after surgery when the potential occurrence of severe postoperative complication is excluded. The limitating factor is the risk of postoperative haemorrhage. However, the Austrian DRGsystem and the performance-based hospital financing do not allow cost-effectiveness for a shortened hospital stay in thyroid surgery. Methodik. A perineal approach to treating rectal prolapse is ideal for frail patients. Internal rectal prolapse has been successfully treated with transanal resection using the Contour + Transtar TM . This technique has been modified to the perineal stapled prolapse resection (PSP), a new procedure for external rectal prolapse. Methods. From July 2007 to November 2007 8 female patients unsuited to transabdominal treatment of rectal prolapse were recruited prospectively for PSP. Doing PSP the prolapse was first opened longitudinally with a straight stapler and then resected step by step 2 cm proximal to the dentate line with a curved reloadable stapler. Feasibility, complications and reinterventions of the procedure were assessed. Results. In all patients PSP was performed without intraoperative complications. The median operating time was 32.5 min (range: 22-45). To resect the prolapse six stapler-cartridges (5-8) were needed. The median specimen weighted 79 g (25-132) and measured 85 mm (60-150) in length. A moderate bleeding occurred after starting anticoagulation in a patient with artificial heart valve 5 days postoperatively. The bleeding stopped without intervention after reducing the anticoagulation. At follow-up, all patients were well and showed no early recurrence of prolapse. Conclusions. PSP is a safe and easy surgery to perform for rectal prolapse. Functional results and long-term recurrence rate must be investigated further. Methodik.
