Global protein expression analysis (proteomics) has emerged as an exciting novel technology recently successfully applied to several fields of medicine. However, no data are currently available that investigated patients undergoing bariatric surgery by means of serum proteomics. Methods. Sixteen morbidly obese patients (11 females, 5 males; BMI >40 kg=m 2 ; mean age 41.5 AE 10.2 years) were included in this study. All patients underwent laparoscopic adjustable gastric banding. Serum protein expression analysis pre-and postoperatively was performed using fluorescence two-dimensional difference gel electrophoresis (2D-DIGE). Spots of interest were subjected to nanospray ionization tandem mass spectrometry (MS= MS) and the spectra were then searched against SwissProt database. Expression of selected proteins was confirmed by Western blot analysis. Results. Mean follow up after gastric banding was 998 AE 207 days. Significant weight reduction was achieved in all patients. Serum 2D-DIGE enabled to identify a total of 1132 protein spots. For 110 of these protein spots, the expression level pre-operatively was more than twofold different from that observed post-operatively. Spots with highly significant differential regulation identified with MS=MS were derived from coagulation factor-II, alpha-2-macroglobulin, serine-proteinase-inhibitor, complement component-4B, hemopexin, cystatin-A, ceruloplasmin, catenin, apolipoprotein-A-I and inter-alpha-inhibitor-protein-H4. Most excitingly, the protein with highest altered regulation (>5-fold) was identified as apolipoprotein A-IV, a recently described hypothalamic satiety factor involved in the control of food intake and body weight regulation. Conclusions. This is the first clinical 2D-DIGE study demonstrating that serum proteomics might hold great potential for eminent insights into metabolic regulations pre and post surgical interventions in morbidly obese patients. Long-term results after laparoscopic adjustible gastric banding in adolescent patients Background. During the last years increasing numbers of children have been reported with a body mass index (BMI) higher than the 85 th percentile in the western world. Surgical strategies are still discussed controversially in adolescent patients, because of the impact on further maturing process. Laparoscopic adjustable gastric banding (LAGB) is considered as a minimal invasive procedure without alterations on the physiological behaviour of the bowel and therefore favoured as first choice surgical bariatric treatment in adolescent patients. Methods. Between 1998 and 2004 50 adolescent patients were treated with LAGB due to a BMI higher than 30 kg=m 2 . The surgical procedure was performed at three highly experienced centers for Bariatric Surgery. Mean age was 17.1 AE 2.2 years (range 9 to 20 years) at time of surgery. Follow-up investigations were performed in the outpatients clinic of the treating hospitals. Psychological changes were analysed by the BAROS questionnaire. Results. The mean BMI decreased from 45.2 AE 7.6 kg=m 2 at time of surgery to 31.5 AE 10.2 kg=m 2 after a mean follow up of 56.8 AE 18.8 months (32.6 AE 6.8 kg=m 2 after 34.7 AE 17.5 months FU, p ¼ 0.5). Excessive weight loss was 71.8 AE 39.0%. Quality of life improved significantly between 3 to 5 years after operation (BAROS: 5.5 AE 1.9 increased to 6.3 AE 2.2, p ¼ 0.01). All preoperative comorbidities resolved in patients with functioning band. Conclusions. The determining weight loss results within the first 3 years after surgery and weight remains stable in patients with functioning band thereafter. Perioperative comorbidities resolve within the first 5 years after treatment. In case of LAGB failure gastric bypass has to be considered even in adolescents. Laparoscopic adjustable gastric banding in older patients: the ideal technique? Background. The population of Western countries is increasingly overweight and aging. For morbid obesity, bariatric surgery is so far the only effective therapeutic option to achieve durable weight loss. Patients over 55 years were however denied surgery in many centers because of their higher operative risk. In Europe, Laparoscopic Adjustable Gastric Banding (LAGB) has emerged as the primary technique in bariatric surgery. LAGB is probably better suited to older morbidly obese patients than more invasive methods. We undertook a retrospective study of patients older than 55 years who received LAGB at our institution. Methods. Between 1997 and 2007, a total of 303 patients underwent LAGB at our department. Of these, 50 patients were over 55-year-old. These patients were compared with the 253 LAGB patients younger than 55 years. The two groups were not different in median BMI, m : f ratio, or duration of surgery. Results. The percentage of patients over 55 years increased steadily over the ten years observed. Excessive weight loss in patients over 55 years was faster and more persistent. Severe and minor operative complications were comparable while younger patients suffered more port complications and more secondary abdominal procedures related to weight loss (such as cholecystectomy). Conclusions. Laparoscopic adjustable gastric banding can be performed in patients over 55 years with better success and comparable complication rates. This is probably due to the better compliance in older patients. Obviously, the little invasive technique of LAGB is better suited to older patients and therefore increasingly chosen by surgeons. Efficacy of bariatric surgery in the treatment of obesity-related type II Diabetes mellitus Background. Up to 80% of the diabetes mellitus type 2 population are overweight. Effective weight control can lead to improvement or even resolution of diabetes. Bariatric surgery represents a suitable option for sustained weight loss in severely obese-diabetic subjects. Conservative treatment results in reduced weight loss for diabetic patients when compared to a non-diabetic control group. There is little evidence whether this difference also exists after bariatric surgery. Methods. The change in the diabetic status and weight loss in 72 (24 m=50 f, BMI 48.1 kg=m 2 ) morbidly obese diabetic subjects undergoing bariatric surgery in a single institution was analysed. Evidence of stable treatment was required with oral antidiabetic agents or insulin. The control group consisted of 72 morbidly obese, non-diabetic patients, matched for age, sex, BMI and type of bariatric procedure. Results. Mean excess weight loss (EWL) was 37.8% after six and 50.3% after 12 months in the diabetic group. In 47 (65.3%) subjects diabetes resolved completely and 25 subjects (34.7%) had significantly improvement of diabetes after 12 months. The control group exhibited an average EWL of 41.6% at 6 months and 53.4% after 12 months. There was no significant difference in weight loss between both groups at 6 and 12 months. Conclusions. Laparoscopic bariatric surgery resulted in significant, sustained weight loss leading to resolution or amelioration of diabetes in almost all patients. Contrary to conservative treatment there was no difference in EWL between the diabetic and non-diabetic group. Key words. bariatric surgery, excess weight loss, diabetes mellitus. Sleeve gastrectomy as a first step or definitive bariatric procedure Background. Sleeve gastrectomy (SG) represents a modern technique in bariatric surgery. It may be applied as first step procedure in the superobese or as a definitive operation. Methods. From 2003 to 2007 50 sleeve gastrectomies were performed as primary bariatric operations. Thirty-five operations were planned as definitive procedures; 15 operations were performed as first step operations because of massive or visceral obesity. Results. One (2%) surgical complication (leakage of staple line) occurred and had to be treated by a reoperation . There was no mortality. On follow-up patients lost weight significantly. Four patients after planned definitive SG (11% 4=35) had to be reoperated (conversion to Roux-Y gastric bypass) because of severe reflux (2 patients) or inadequate weight loss (2 patients). Patients after first step SG demonstrated significant reductions of overweight. Until now two patients have been converted to Roux-Y gastric bypass after SG without problems. Conclusions. Sleeve gastrectomy represents is a safe and effective operation for morbid obesity and is an excellent first step procedure for superobese patients. GIGIP 2 -Gesellschaft für Implantologie und Gewebeintegrierte Prothetik: Ästhetik in der rekonstruktiven Chirurgie Esthetic and functional results after reconstruction of the oral cavity C. Schaudy, H. Haider, K. Vinzenz The fact that the basis for important functional aspects like speaking, mastication, deglutition and an effortless respiration are localized in the maxillofacial area, the aim of any treatment must always be the most possible lifelike restoration. Especially in orofacial surgery anatomic form, function and esthetics present an inseparable unit with any deflection in reconstructive and aesthetic surgery resulting in camouflage of the respective disease. The anatomy of the: midface region is mainly characterized by mucosa covered, subtle yet mechanically stable bone and dental structures surrounding pneumatized cavities (in particular paranasal sinuses and oral cavity) -the external facial soft tissues fixated with retinaculae to the supporting bone structures. In oral reconstruction all tissue components including bone, attached gingiva and teeth resp. implants must be respected as well if a functional restoration is sought. Osteocutaneous and osteomyocutaneous flaps in the midface region (Swartz et al. 1986 , David et al. 1988 , Thoma et al. 1991 , Forrest et al. 1992 , Hidalgo et al. 1994 , Nakayama et al. 1994 , Reychler et al. 1994 , Schustermann et al. 1994 , Wei et al. 1994 , 2002 , Bähr 1996 , Hayter et al. 1996 , Igawa et al. 1998 , Urken et al. 1998 , Cordeiro et al. 1999 , Kazaoka et al. 1999 , Shpitzer et al. 1999 , Dreschler et al. 2000 are always too bulky and therefor prevent physiological oral and nasal resp. paranasal function. Prelamination of bone with dermis to create a substitute for oral mucosa bypasses the problem introduced when skin grafts and intestinal grafts are used for intraoral rehabilitation (Millesi et al. 1998 (Millesi et al. , 2004 . At the beginning attempts were made to prefabricate single separate flap components like the vascular bundle for lengthening purposes (Kärcher 1991). The current project of this nature is the prefabrication of a ''Custom Vascularised Bone Graft in Man'' by dint of ''tissue engeneering' ' (Warnke et al. 2004) . First attempts to provide an intracavitary lining in the head and neck region were introduced since the mid-nineties. (Rath et al. 1997 , Pribaz et al. 1999 , Delaere et al. 2001 , Jaquet et al. 2004 ). Yet since the evaluation of the aspired clinical results' quality initially oftentimes fell short, a series of new surgical concepts were not able to prevail. Prefabricated complex composite grafts are able to meet the needs for a complete state-of-the-art reconstruction, as they consist of preformed bone, implants and a mucosa like lining, tightly adherent to the bone (Holle et al. 1996 , Vinzenz et al. 1996 , 1997 , 1998 , Igawa et al. 1998 , Rohner et al. 2000 , 2003 , Holle and Vinzenz 2004 . The graphical schema illustrated the principles of the prefabrication of a complex transplant on the left side. In the last years our study group could histologically and immune-histologically confirm the clinical results of our operation technique regarding remodelling activity, attachment of the lining and wet keratin expression of the self-regenerating mucosa (Vinzenz et al. 1998 , Kunstfeld et al. 2001 , Schlenz et al. 2001 ). An excellent alternative approach on the other hand is the craniofacial distraction osteogenesis by use of a bone transport technique. The first clinical application of this technique to the craniofacial skeleton was performed by Constantino and co-workers in 1992=1993 and reported first in 1995 (Constantino et al. 1995 . Bone transport in a distraction osteogenesis technique involving the slow movement of a free segment of bone (transport segment) across an osseous defect that developed as a result of severe congenital deformity, trauma or oncologic resection (Samchukov et al. 2001) . After gradual advancement of the transport segment, new bone tissue forms behind the moving segment, thereby filling the defect with new bone (Fedotov 1998 , Papageorge and Apostolodis 1999 , Stucki-McCormick et al. 1999 , Klein 2001 , Guerrero et al. 2001 . After completion of bone transport and target bone segments to produce fusion at the docking site (Klein 2001). The new bone can subsequently be implanted with dental implants (Odo and Ueda 2001). In addition the method provides new lining by soft tissue expansion of the attached gingival tissue. The so called ''distraction histogenesis'' is a biological process of soft tissue adaptation to gradual stretching (Samchukov et al. 2001 ). On the right side of the graphical schema the principles of distraction osteogenesis is illustrated: The lengthening of tissue structures by distraction. In reconstructive surgery e.g. after radical cancer surgery distraction osteogenesis is mainly applied as bone transport (Vinzenz et al. 2002) . Restoring oral function is achieved by bone anchored bridgework using dental implants. A mucosa supported prosthesis is to be avoided in any case! An attached tension-and inflammation-free neogingiva that permits no displacement against the underlining bone sealing of the implants against the oral environment guarantees their longterm function throughout masticatory loading (Schlenz et al. 2001) . Taking all these aspects into account form, function and esthetics present an inseparable unit. In the presentation several case reports will illustrate this essential correlation. Grundlagen. Die Durchtrennung der Vasa gastricae breves während der Nissen Fundoplikation wird immer noch kontroversiell diskutiert. Das Ziel dieser prospektiv randomisierten Studie bestand darin, den klinischen und funktionellen Verlauf nach Durchtrennung versus Schonung der Vasa gastricae breves im Langzeit Follow-up zu evaluieren. Methodik. 41 konsekutive Patienten (m ¼ 30, w ¼ 11) wurden nach Nissen Fundoplikation prä-und postoperativ (6 Monaten=4-6 Jahre) analysiert. 19 Patienten (Gruppe 1) sind nach Nissen ohne Durchtrennung und 22 Patienten mit Durchtrennung der kurzen Magengefäße fundopliziert worden. Die funktionellen postoperativen Ergebnisse und klinischen Symptome wurden ermittelt. Ergebnisse. Präoperative Symptome (Gruppe1= Gruppe2) waren Sodbrennen (84%=86%), Regurgitation (79%=86%), pulmonale Symptome (47%=45%), Dysphagie (11%=32%), Retrosternale Schmerzen (16%=9%) und Globusgefühl (21%=27%). Präoperativ wiesen 84% (Gruppe 1) und 59% (Gruppe 2) Refluxösophagitis auf. Nach 4-6 Jahren treten Regurgitation in 8% und Dysphagie in 18% (Gruppe 1) auf. Die Dysphagierate in Gruppe 2 fällt nach 6 Monaten auf 17%, um im Langzeitverlauf auf 26% anzusteigen. Die Operationsdauer (Gruppe 1: 1,82 h vs. Gruppe 2: 2,09 h; p < 0,05) und der Blutverlust (Gruppe 1: nicht messbar; Gruppe 2: 25 ml; p < 0,05) zeigten signifikante Unterschiede. Der DeMeester Score sank von 26,6 und 24,7 postoperativ auf 2,2 (Gruppe 1) und 2,5 (Gruppe 2). Der Ruhedruck im LES war postoperativ bei 23,9 mmHg (Gruppe 1) und 24,6 mmHg (Gruppe 2) bei unauffälliger Relaxation. Der Lebensqualitätsindex zeigte keinen statistisch signifikanten Unterschied. Schlussfolgerungen. Die routinemäßige Durchtrennung der Vasa gastricae breves bei der Nissen Fundoplikation ergibt keinen funktionellen oder klinischen Vorteil im Kurz-und Langzeitverlauf, verlängert jedoch die Operationszeit und erhöht den Blutverlust. Hiatushernie mit paraösophagealem Anteil -Ist nach Netzverstärkung eine Fundoplikatio notwendig? Grundlagen. Bei der Sanierung von Hiatushernien (HH) mit paraösophagealem Anteil wird die Fundoplikatio zur Senkung der Rezidivrate empfohlen. Da eine Senkung der Rezidivrate durch Verstärkung des Hiatus mit Kunstoffnetzen gezeigt werde konnte und fundoplikatio-assoziierte Nebenwirkungen nicht selten sind, stellt sich die Frage, ob nach Netzverstärkung eine Fundoplikatio notwendig ist. Methodik. Prospektive Erfassung aller Patienten mit paraösophagealer und gemischter Hiatushernie, die zwischen 2001 und 2006 unselektioniert mittels laparoskopisch mesh-augmentierter Hiatoplastik (LMAH) behandelt wurden. Nach Hernienreposition und dorsaler Crurorraphie erfolgt bei der LMAH eine zirkuläre Netzverstärkung mit abschliessender anteriorer Cardiofundophrenikopexie. Präoperativ und ein Jahr postoperativ wurden Symptome mittels Symptomfragebogen (GSRS) erfasst sowie HH und Ö sophagitisstadium endoskopisch ermittelt. Ergebnisse. Von 34 operierten Patienten hatten präoperativ 13 (38%) eine paraösophageale und 21 (62%) eine gemischte HH, 16 (47%) Patienten hatten eine Ö sophagitis. Für das 1 Jahres Follow-up standen 32 (94%) Patienten zur Verfügung. Vier (12,5%) Patienten hatten ein axiales Hernienrezidiv, bei 4 (12,5%) Patienten zeigte sich neu eine Ö sophagitis. Neun (28,1%) Patienten benötigten Protonenpumperhemmer. Netzkomplikationen traten keine auf. Der mittlere Refluxscore fiel von 2,9 auf 1,6 (p < 0,01), Gasbloat von 2,9 auf 1,8 (p < 0,01) und Dysphagie von 1,8 auf 1,2 (p ¼ 0,07). Ein Patient war unfähig Luft aufzustossen, Erbrechen war für zwei Patienten unmöglich. 94% der Patienten beurteilten das Operationsresultat als ,,gut bis ausgezeichnet'' und würden sich wieder operieren lassen. Schlussfolgerungen. Bei HH mit paraösophagealem Anteil scheint ein Repair mit Netzverstärkung ohne Fundoplikatio (LMAH) möglich zu sein. Langzeitergebnisse bezüglich Rezidivrate, Refluxkontrolle und Netzkomplikationen sind abzuwarten. Background. Laparoscopic antireflux surgery (LARS) may fail to control reflux and result in a high rate of postoperative dysphagia in patients with gastroesophageal reflux disease (GERD) and preoperative manometrically intact lower esophageal sphincter (LES). We sought to determine the impact of the preoperative LES function on outcomes one year after LARS. Methods. Three hundred and fifty one patients with GERD who underwent consecutive LARS were evaluated before and one year after surgery. The intraabdominal length (LES-IAL) and the pressure of the LES (LES-P) were determined by esophageal manometry. The study population was divided into into 4 groups according to the preoperative LES-IAL and LES-P. Baseline and follow-up data of upper gastrointestinal endoscopy, barium swallow esophagogram, 24-hour esophageal pH-monitoring and quality of life were collected prospectively. Results. Preoperatively 6.3% of the patients had a manometrically intact LES. Fifty-six percent of the patients had an intraabdominal length of <1 cm and 74% had a resting pressure of <8 mmHg. The preoperative manometric character of the LES did not impact frequency and=or severity of reflux symptoms, quality of life and DeMeester scores postoperatively. Conclusions. All symptoms, reflux scores and quality of life improved significantly after LARS independent of the preoperative function of the LES. Normal preoperative esophageal manometry does not cause higher rates of dysphagia after LARS. Therefore, routine preoperative manometry may be not essential in GERD patients. The challenge of diagnostic assessment of a failed fundoplication: benefits of highresolution manometry of the GE-junction Background. Although upper endoscopy, and barium esophagography often reveal anatomic abnormalities in patients following failed fundoplication, functional information allowing insight into the cause of recurrent symptoms is key to clinical decisions. High resolution manometry (HRM) is a novel, imaged based technology which may yield superior results than conventional manometry in this setting. Aim. To study the high resolution manometric characteristics of postfundoplication patients with dysphagia. Methods. Study population: 17 patients with foregut symptoms following fundoplication (2005) (2006) (2007) . Symptoms: dysphagia in 12=17 (71%), regurgitation in 9 (53%), heartburn in 4 (24%), cough in 3 (18%), vomiting in 2 (12%), chest-pain in 5 (29%) and bloating in 1 (6%). Studies were analyzed with particular attention to characteristics of the neo-high pressure zone. Endoscopy revealed a failed fundoplication in 13=17 patients, 4 patients had no apparent anatomic changes. Results. Percent LES relaxation was significantly lower (31.4 vs. 76.1), and LES residual pressure was significantly higher (12.1 vs. 6.1) in post-fundoplication patients. Eighty eight percent of the patients had lower than normal intra-abdominal LES lengths. A majority (59%) of post-fundoplication patients had abnormal double-peaked waves suggesting outflow obstruction. The percent LES relaxation in postfundoplication patients with dysphagia was significantly lower than in patients with other symptoms. Conclusions. HRM revealed high residual pressures and low percent LES relaxations of the neo-high pressure zone in virtually all patients with post-fundoplication dysphagia. Further this measure correlated with the presence of dysphagia. HRM allows clinically useful observations in the evaluation of complex esophageal pathology. Association of gastroesophageal reflux and O 2 desaturation in patients with GERD; A novel study of simultaneous 24-hour impedance-pH and continuous pulse-oximetry Background. Respiratory symptoms are present in up to 50% of GERD patients. The aim of this study was to assess the association of gastroesophageal reflux with O 2 desaturation in patients with and without respiratory symptoms using combined simultaneous ambulatory monitoring systems. Methods. The study population consisted of 11 GERD patients in which 443 reflux episodes were detected by MII-pH study. Eight patients had primary respiratory symptoms and 3 typical symptoms (heartburn and regurgitation). All patients underwent simultaneous 24 hr MII-pH and O 2 saturation monitoring via ambulatory reflux and pulse-oximetry monitoring. A reflux-desaturation association was considered present if O 2 desaturation occurred within 30 seconds prior to or 10 min after a reflux event. Results. Three hundred and thirty eight reflux events occurred in patients with primary respiratory symptoms and 105 in those with typical GERD symptoms. Nearly 60% of these 443 reflux events were associated with O 2 desaturation. Markedly more events were associated with O 2 desaturation in patients with respiratory symptoms (68%, 229=338) than in patients with typical reflux symptoms (25%, 26=105, p < 0.01). The difference in reflux-desaturation association was even more profound when proximal reflux events were compared, occurring in 76% (130=171) of patients with respiratory symptoms vs. 14% (8=56) of those with typical GERD symptoms (p < 0.01). Conclusions. There is a remarkably high prevalence of oxygen desaturation associated with esophageal acidification in patients with primary respiratory symptoms. This may prove to be a useful diagnostic test in this difficult group of patients. Endoscopy, squamocolumnar junction histopathology and multichannel intraluminal impedance-pH-monitoring of the esophagus Background. Endoscopically visible CLE and esophagitis are absent in many patients with clinical GERD. Aim of this study was to correlate endoscopic-bioptic findings with results of multichannel-intraluminal-impedance and pH-monitoring (MII-pH) of the esophagus. Methods. Fifty-four GERD patients (30 males, 51 AE 11.9 a) prospectively underwent endoscopy with biopsies from the squamocolumnar junction and from visible CLE, defined as presence of gastric type mucosa proximal to the commencement of rugal folds. Esophagitis and CLE were graded according to the Los Angeles classification and the Paull-Chandrasoma classification respectively. MII-pH was performed off antisecretory medication. Results. Diagnostic yield of endoscopic, histopathologic and MII-pH parameters see Tab. 1. In 5 patients intestinal metaplasia (IM) was detected in biopsy specimens obtained from an endoscopically normal squamocolumnar junction. 4 of these patients had a positive SI. A positive correlation was found between the presence of endoscopically visible CLE and the number of liquid containing refluxes (R ¼ 0.31, p ¼ 0.022). Conclusions. Histopathologic detection of CLE in biopsies obtained from the squamocolumnar junction was the most sensitive diagnostic procedure to diagnose GERD, followed by a positive symptom index during MII-pH. Presence of endoscopically visible CLE was correlated with the number or liquid containing refluxes, but not acid exposure or presence of esophagitis. The clinical and oncologic relevance of CLE detected at the squamocolumnar junction only needs to be defined. Significant pressure differences between solid-state and water perfused systems in lower esophageal sphincter measurement Background. To compare lower esophageal sphincter (LES) measurements obtained with water-perfused manometry with a solid-state technique. Normal values for LES resting pressure in suspected GERD (gastroesophageal reflux disease) -patients have been established using water-perfused manometry. These standardvalues are also applied using solid-state techniques, although they have never been compared before. Methods. Thirty healthy subjects were studied twice on the same day: technique 1: Station pull through using a water perfused catheter with ports arranged at 0, 90, 180 and 270 degrees which were averaged to give a mean LES pressure. Technique 2: Solid-state circumferential probe with a single station pull through. Data were collected using the same computer system and program. The LES pressures were randomly and blindly analyzed. Results. Twenty-eight subjects of 30 were analyzed. Using the solid state system, the mean LES pressure was higher (26.6 vs. 21.7 mmHg, p < 0.02) and 24 of 28 (85%) individual measurements were higher. The correlation between the two sets of measurements was also poor (r ¼ 0.54). Two subjects had a hypertensive LES by solid state (53.4 and 41.9 mmHg) while their pressures were normal with water perfused manometry (19.4 and 23.4 mmHg). The distal esophageal pressures (mean of pressure at 3 and 8 cm above LES) were the same with the two techniques. Conclusions. In normal control subjects LES measurement using circumferential solid-state transducers yields higher pressures than standard water perfused manometric measurement. Which system yields the more accurate measurement of the physiologic LES remains to be determined. Background. HRM introduces NASA technology into the diagnostic field of esophageal motility disorders with 36 sensors along a manometry catheter covering the foregut from the pharynx to the stomach. Converted into tempo-spatial pressure plots displaying pressure changes in real time, HRM allows to discover early motility changes, where conventional diagnostic methods might not be sensitive enough. After establishing normal values in 50 healthy volunteers, this technology is now being tested in clinical routine and compared to endoscopy and barium swallow. Methods. Patients with symptoms of esophageal motility disorders (EMD) underwent HRM with 10 swallows of 5 ml water in supine position. Systematic questionnaire to evaluate patients symptoms were compared to the results of HRM, endoscopy and barium swallow. Results. Application of HRM is easy and save to use in daily routine. Results are reproducible and interpretation user independent compared to conventional manometry. The procedure can be used repetitively without greater risk compared to endoscopy or fluoroscopy. The newly designed software changes the approach from pure numbers into a visual barium swallow like appearance, which allows a more complete view into the swallowing act and its pathophysiological changes occurring in a vast number of diseases. Conclusions. Although the technology just started to develop from a research tool into a useful diagnostic test in daily routine, it already shows great impact on patient treatment. With its new visual approach, HRM helps to understand pathophysiological changes in esophageal motility disorders better than endoscopy and barium swallow alone. Background. Dysphagia is a common symptom in patients with gastro-esophageal reflux (GERD) and after antireflux surgery. Aim of this study was to evaluate whether a Multichannel Intraluminal Impedance and pH (MII-pH) system can be used to assess esophageal transport function and its relation to dysphagia. Methods. Fourty-three GERD patients (17 males, age 48.5 AE 12.6 a) underwent esophageal manometry and a MII transport test. Series of 10 swallows a 5 ml saline and a viscous gel were investigated in supine and sitting body position respectively. Bolus transport was considered complete if impedance dropped to <50% from baseline after a swallow and recovered in every tracing. Results. Thirty-nine interpretable results of the MII transport test were obtained. In 4 patients (1 eosiniphilic esophagitis, 2 long segment Barrett esophagus, 1 thoracically herniated fundoplication) bolus movement could not be assessed due to low baseline. Significantly less viscous boli in both body positions and liquid boli in supine position were completely transported through the esophagus in dysphagia patients than in those without this symptom (Tab. 1). LES resting pressure (16.4 vs. 16.8 mmHg), LES residual pressure upon swallowing (6.7 vs. 6.0 mm Hg) and contraction amplitudes in the distal (61 vs. 84 mmHg), middle (60 vs. 64 mmHg) and proximal third of the esophagus (40 vs. 48 mmHg) did not differ significantly between dysphagia and no dysphagia patients. Conclusions. MII is useful for the evaluation of esophageal transport in GERD patients. In contrast to manometry the MII transport test significantly differed between dysphagia and nondysphagia patients. Background. The impact of body position on esophageal function and pathogenesis of gastroesophageal reflux disease (GERD) are unclear. We tested the effect of body position on esophageal manometry. Methods. Forty-six persons (47 AE 14 years, 25 females) with GERD symptoms prospectively underwent station-pull-throughmanometry in supine and left lateral recumbent position using a solid-state catheter (Koenigsberg Instruments, Pasadena, CA). Characteristics of lower esophageal sphincter (LES) function and esophageal body motility were assessed. Results. LES characteristics significantly differed between supine and left lateral position (Tab. 1). Location of the respiratory inversion point (RIP) and length of the esophageal body were not affected by body position. Our findings indicate that the difference in LES length mainly resulted from shortening of the abdominal LES portion. Conclusions. LES competence and esophageal body performance were significantly impaired in left lateral recumbent position compared to supine position. Thus, body position dependent changes of esophageal function are suggested to contribute to GERD pathophysiology. Background. Discrepancy exists between the endoscopic (rugal folds) and the histopathologic definition (oxyntic mucosa) of proximal stomach. We compared endoscopy and histopathology of the esophagogastric junction in patients with gastroesophageal reflux disease (GERD). Methods. One hundred and two consecutive patients (60 females) with GERD prospectively underwent endoscopy including multi level biopsy sampling at the level of the rise of rugal folds ( ¼ level 0), and 0.5, 1.0 cm distal and 0.5, > 1 cm proximal to this point. Columnar lined esophagus (CLE) and esophagitis were cataloged according to the histopathologic Paull-Chandrasoma and endoscopic Los Angeles classification, respectively. Hiatal hernia was assessed if the endoscopic rugal folds commenced > 2 cm above the diaphragm; competency of the esophagogastric valve was graded according to the Hill classification. Results. All patients had histopathologic CLE with maximal presence at level 0 (97%) and decrease towards proximal and distal biopsy levels (81%, 28%, 40% and 18% at levels À0.5, À1.0, þ0.5, þ1.0 cm, respectively). Histopathologic CLE was longer than endoscopic CLE (p > 0.05). None of the patients had dysplasia or carcinoma. Conclusions. In GERD patients the esophagogastric junction cannot be assessed by endoscopy but requires histopathology of multi-level biopsies. The squamocolumnar junction harbors the highest yield for assessment of intestinal metaplasia. Notfalltherapie der akuten Hb-wirksamen Blutung im oberen Gastrointestinaltrakt Grundlagen. Die akute Blutung im OGI ist selten mit einer Inzidenz von 100=100.000 Einwohner=Jahr. Trotz breiter Verfügbarkeit von endoskopischen und operativen Möglichkeiten ist sie mit einer hohen Letalität vergesellschaftet. Ursachen der hohen Morbidität und Letalität werden analysiert. Methodik. In den vergangenen 5 Jahren wurden an unserer Klinik 59 Patienten wegen einer akuten OGI-Blutung behandelt. In 31 Fällen (52%) fand sich ein Magenulcus, in je 5 Fällen war die Blutungsquelle eine Schleimhauterosion des Magens bzw. eine Mallory Weis Läsion. Seltenere Blutungsquellen waren Anastomosen des OGI-Traktes (n ¼ 4), biliodigestive Anastomosen (n ¼ 2) und einer Pankreatikojejunostomie (n ¼ 1). Ergebnisse. In 45 Fällen erfolgte eine endoskopische Intervention, die in 27 Fällen (60%) erfolgreich war. In den übrigen 18 Fällen (40%) war eine Operation notwendig. In 14 Fällen (24%) erfolgte primär eine Operation. Die gesamte Liegedauer betrug 17 AE 9 Tage (MW AE Standardabweichung). Operative Revisionen waren bei 13 von 32 Patienten notwendig (41%). Die Gesamtletalität betrug 27%. Schlussfolgerungen. Trotz in 60% d.F. primär erfolgreicher endoskpischer Intervention ist die Letalität auch heute noch sehr hoch. Eine frühzeitigere chirurgische Intervention kann möglicherweise dazu beitragen, dass künftig die Letalität gesenkt wird. Unverzichtbar ist ein konsequentes postinterventionelles Monitoring des Patienten mit der Möglichkeit der unverzüglichen endoskopischen oder operativen Reintervention. Bei endoskopisch nicht sicher suffizient zu stillender Blutung sollte die OP-Indikation aggressiver und unter (noch) stabilen Herzkreislaufverhältnissen gestellt werden, um die hohe Gesamtletalität zu senken. Grundlagen. Der sichere und effiziente endoskopische Verschluß von Colotomien ist die Grundvorraussetzung fuer zukuenftige endoscopische transcolonische intraperitoneale Operationen, endoskopische Colon-Vollwandexzisionen und fuer den Verschluss von Colonperforationen, will man laparoskopische oder offene Eingriffe vermeiden. Ziel der Studie war es, den Verschluss einer Colotomie mit dem TAS (Tissue Approximation System; Ethicon, Inc.), einem Prototypen zum endoskopischen Verschluss von Enterotomien, zu erproben und mit dem Verschluss mittels laparoskopischer fortlaufender Naht zu vergleichen. Methodik. An 16 Schweinen wurden 2-3 cm haltende Colotomien laparoskopisch durchgefuehrt. In 8 dieser Tiere erfolgte der Verschluss rein endoskopisch mit dem TAS, waehrend in den uebrigen 8 Tieren in der Kontrollgruppe der Verschluss mit einer fortlaufenden laparoskopischen Naht durchgefuehrt wurde. Die Tiere wurden nach 2 Wochen euthanasiert und obduziert. Endpunkte der Studie waren das Erreichen eines erfolgreichen Verschlusses, Verschlusszeiten, postoperative Infektionen und Komplikationen. Ergebnisse. Alle Colotomien konnten in beiden Gruppen erfolgreich verschlossen werden. Mediane Verschlusszeiten waren 39,5 min (25-95 min) in der TAS Gruppe und 23 min (16-40 min) in der laparoskopischen Gruppe (p ¼ 0,013). Es gab keine intra-oder postoperativen Komplikationen. Bei der Obduktion waren alle Colotomien gut verheilt und es fanden sich keine Hinweise auf Peritonitis oder intraabdominelle Abszesse. Schlussfolgerungen. Der endoskopische Verschluss von Colotomien konnte sicher und effizient mit dem TAS durchgefuehrt werden. Abgesehen von einer laengeren Verschlusszeit, welche im Rahmen der Lernkurve verkuerzt werden kann, sind die Ergebnisse mit der laparoskopischen Technik vergleichbar. Das TAS koennte auch im Menschen als Instrument zum endoskopischen Verschluss von Colotomien und Colonperforationen dienen. Background. Background. Splenic artery aneurysms (SAA) are the most common visceral artery aneurysms with an incidence of up to 10% in the eldery population. Treatment with endovascular exclusion, if feasible, or surgical excision should be considered in aneuysms larger than 2 cm in diameter. Methods. Laparoscopic aneurysm excision has been described for distal SAAs, however, if the main trunk of the splenic artery is affected, often preservation of splenic bloodflow is not feasible. Results. We describe the case of a 35-year female patient, who presented with abdominal discomfort to our department. Computed tomography revealed a distal splenic artery aneurysm with a maximum diameter of 2.8 cm, which seemed amendable by laparoscopic resection. Using a four trochar technique, after takedown of the left colonic flexure and identification of the upper border of the pancreatic tail, the aneurysm was approached from the splenic hilus and isolated. Intraoperative sonography revealed sufficient splenic blood flow through the short gastric arteries, and the SAA was excised. Without postoperative morbidity, the patient was discharged on postoperative day 3. Conclusions. Laparoscopic resection of distal splenic artery aneurysms with preservation of the spleen is feasible when intraoperative imaging of splenic blood-flow identifies sufficient collateral flow through the short gastric arteries. Background. The most severe complication following performance of an intestinal anastomosis is the breakdown of this construction. The clinical condition of a patient is not always conform with the existence of an anastomosis leakage, therefore a sensitive marker like the c-reactice protein (CRP) is needed for early detection of an inflammatory event, especially anastomosis dehiscence. Our paper poses the question whether the postoperative monitoring measuring the CRP is sensitive enough for an early detection of an anastomosis dehiscence. Methods. During the past five years, all surgical procedures of the lower intestine were examined where a construction of a primary anastomosis was necessary and a dehiscence of an anastomosis occured. In these complicated cases, the postoperative course of the CRP was evaluated and contrasted with the control group which demonstrated an uneventful course. Results. We analyse whether an anastomosis dehiscence always correlates with an increased CRP and we present cases where the CRP demonstrated a decreasing course, but a leakage was still present and we try to answer the question whether postoperative monitoring measuring the CRP can detect early an anastomosis break down. Conclusions. Because of the high mortality and morbidity of an anastomosis dehiscence, the early detection of this complication is very important. The c-reactive protein can be used as a sensitive marker for the existence of a leakage, but as we will show, it is not always sensitive enough to detect a beginning complicated course and sometimes it even seems to be increased without an apparent reason. Methodik. In einer kleinen retrospektiven Analyse vergleichen wir sechs ,,matched pairs'', also insgesamt 12 Patienten, die wegen diffuser Peritonitis an der Intensivstation behandelt wurden. Bei jeweils der Hälfte davon wurde entweder nur eine naso-gastrale Sonde eingelegt, oder zusätzlich und neben dieser eine naso-jejunale Ernährungssonde platziert. In weiteren 7 Fällen haben wir diese zweite Sonde endoskopisch platziert, um nach dem Versagen aller anderen prokinetischen Maßnahmen eine Relaparotomie zu vermeiden. Ergebnisse. 1. Bei alleiniger naso-gastraler Sonde dauerte es bis zum ersten Stuhlgang im Median 5,5 (3, (5) (6) (7) (8) (9) (10) (11) Tage. Wenn schon intraoperativ zusätzlich eine naso-jejunale Ernährungssonde gelegt wurde, verkürzte sich diese Zeit auf median 4,0 (1, (5) (6) (7) 5) Tage. Dieser Unterschied ist auf Grund der geringen Fallzahlen nicht signifikant, stellt aber einen sehr vorteilhaften Trend dar. 2. In allen Fällen, in denen die naso-jejunale Sonde über das flexible Endoskop platziert wurde, konnte mit anschließender Gabe eines nicht-ionischen Kontrastmittels bzw. von Mannit 20% die Peristaltik in Gang gebracht und das drohende Kompartment-Syndrom abgewendet werden. Mit den handelsüblichen Mother-Baby-Systemen (Sonde in der Sonde) sind diese guten Ergebnisse nicht zu erzielen, da eine ausreichende Dekompression des Magens nur selten erreicht wird. Schlussfolgerungen. Unsere Ergebnisse bedürfen der Bestätigung durch eine randomisierte Studie, die derzeit anläuft. Trotzdem empfehlen wir schon jetzt, bei schweren Peritonitiden gleich intra-operativ neben der üblichen ,,Magensonde'' über das zweite Nasenloch eine naso-jejunale Ernährungssonde einzulegen. Dies kann und soll als ultima ratio auch auf endoskopischem Wege an der Intensivstation erfolgen, wenn der Patient wegen eines protrahierten postoperativen Ileus vor der Relaparaotomie steht. Time and technique of delayed closure of the abdominal wall 2nd Department of Surgery, Wilhelminenspital, Vienna, Austria Background. The aim of this prospective controlled trial is to define the optimal timepoint for delayed closure after vacuum assisted closure (VAC) in the treatment of the open abdomen (OA) in septic patients after abdominal surgery. The delayed closure of the abdominal wall after abdominal VAC treatment is currently a problem due to the high tension of sutures due to the lateralisation of the edges of the fascia. We present early results of an innovative combination of VAC with a new fascialapproximation technique using dynamic fascial sutures (DFS) and delayed closure of the abdominal wall. Methods. During the first surgical procedure using VACtechnique the fascia in the midline are approximated with a running suture of elastic vessel loop. At final closure the abdomen can be closed in the midline using a running nonresorbable suture. Results. Nine patients (6 mens and 3 womens) suffering from an open abdomen following surgery for secondary peritonitis were treated with VAC and DFS. Delayed closure was achieved in all patients after 8.12 (2-23) days and 4.12 (2-10) number of revisions. One superficial and one deep wound infection occured in two patients. We recorded no technique-specific complication. No incisional hernia occured up to this point. Conclusions. Using a new technique combining VAC and DFS in the treatment of the OA, the delayed wound closure by tension-less running suture of the fascia after can be achieved easily without the risk of bursting abdominal walls and incisional hernias. Iatrogene vaskuläre Läsionen im Rahmen der orthopädischen Chirurgie sind äußerst selten (Literaturangaben schwanken zwischen 0,05 und 0,2%). Falls nicht rechtzeitig erkannt und behandelt bedrohen sie zumindest die betroffene Extremität, oft aber auch das Leben des Patienten. Will man iatrogene Gefäßläsionen einteilen kann man zwischen Blutung, Ischämie, einer Kombination aus den beiden letztgenannten Ereignissen und dem Pseudoaneurysma unterscheiden. In diesem Ü bersichtsvortrag werden die häufigsten orthopädischen Zugänge zur prothetischen Versorgung der großen Gelenke und in der Wirbelsäulenchirurgie behandelt. Es wird das anatomische Naheverhältnis zum Gefäßband demonstriert. Die prä-operative Untersuchung sollte auch einen Gefäßstatus beinhalten. Hier wird die Wertigkeit der einzelnen nicht invasiven Untersuchungstechniken diskutiert. Anhand einer Literaturrecherche der letzten Jahre werden die für die einzelnen operativen Techniken typischen Gefäßläsionen aufgezeigt. Einzelne operative Manöver sind mit spezifischen Risiken für die Gefäße behaftet. Diese werden im einzelnen vorgestellt. Um zur Behandlung einer etwaigen Komplikation keine Zeit zu verlieren sollten bei entsprechendem Verdacht schon weiterführende diagnostische Maßnahmen veranlasst werden. Es wird versucht hier einen möglichst allgemein gültigen diagnostischen und therapeutischen Entscheidungspfad vorzustellen. Beim Studium der Literatur zeigt sich, dass auch an großen Zentren etwa die Hälfte der Gefäßläsionen bei orthopädischen Eingriffen erst mit einer Verzögerung von mindestens 24 Stunden entdeckt werden. So muss also vor allem dem Faktor Zeit -der das Behandlungsergebnis nach derartigen Ereignissen massiv beeinflusst -höchste Aufmerksamkeit geschenkt werden. Background. Peritoneal carcinomatosis until recently were considered incurable. Interdisciplinary multimodal therapy including extensive cytoreductive surgery followed by hyperthermic intraperitoneal chemotherapy (HIPEC) offers significant survival benefit. So far, no radiomorphological imaging can predict the intraoperative tumor load. Combined FDG-PET-CT-scan might offer an impact on patient selection, because its findings might influence making the decision for peritonectomy and HIPEC. We evaluated the results of preoperative FDG-PET-CTscan by correlating the findings of metabolic imaging with the intraoperative findings of patients who underwent peritonectomy and HIPEC. Methods. Eleven consecutive patients (mean age: 61, 45 years) underwent preoperative FDG-PET-scans, followed by cytoreduc-tive surgery and HIPEC. The intraperitoneal tumor load was assessed preoperatively by FDG-PET-CT-scan according to the Peritoneal-Carcinomatosis-Index (PCI-PET-CT) according to the intraoperative PCI reported by Sugarbaker (PCI-Sugarbaker). Both indices (PCI-PET-CT and PCI-Sugarbaker) underwent correlation analysis. Moreover we divided the abdominal quadrants into 4 regions (1: upper abdomen, 2: middle abdomen, 3: lower abdomen-pelvis, 4: intestine including jejunum and ileum) and correlated again the different regions. Results. The PCI-PET-CT (mean: 20.54 AE 12.18) was statistically significant correlated with the PCI-Sugarbaker (mean: 21.09 AE 12.8) (r 2 ¼ 0.929; p < 0.0001). In addition, this correlation could be found in respect to the 4 PCI subgroups (upper abdomen: r 2 ¼ 0.765; p ¼ 0.006; middle abdomen: r 2 ¼ 0.779; p ¼ 0.005; lower abdomen-pelvis: r 2 ¼ 0.746; p ¼ 0.008 and intestine: r 2 ¼ 0.862; Conclusions. The PCI-FDG-PET-CT correlates well with the intraoperative Peritoneal-Carcinomatosis-Index by Sugarbaker. Further studies are warranted investigating the potential impact of FDG-PET-CT on preoperative patient selection for peritonectomy and HIPEC in patients suffering from peritoneal carcinomatosis. Background. Combining Bevacizumab with XELOX= FOLFOX4 is inreasingly being recognized as state of the art in the neoadjuvant treatment of colorectal cancer liver metastases. Our group has recently shown that Bevacizumab does not increase perioperative morbidity after surgical resection of colorectal cancer liver metastases. Furthermore, we have shown recently that XELOX=FOLFOX4 causes profound morphological changes in liver parenchyma with Sinusiodal Dilatation and Liverfibrosis as its pathohistological corelate. The aim of this study was to determine if the addition of Bevacizumab does change the injury pattern of XELOX= FOLFOX4. Methods. Liver specimen of 56 patients receiving biweekly bevacizumab plus capecitabine and oxaliplatin for six cycles ( the sixth cycle of therapy did not including bevacizumab) and liver specimen of 50 patients solely receiving capecitabine and oxaliplatin (XELOX) or 5-fluorouracil, leucovorin plus oxaliplatin (FOLFOX4) for six cycles were analyzed. Results. Steatosis, fibrosis, concomitant necroinflammation as well as sinusoidal injury were evaluated according to widely accepted pathohistological scores. We found no difference in grading of steatohepatitis among the two groups. The incidence of sinusoidal dilation of any grade was significantly lower in patients treated with Bevacizumab. Furthermore, the incidence of moderate or severe sinusoidal dilation was significantly higher in paitnes treated without Bevacizumab. Conclusions. We conclude that the addition of Bevacizumab to XELOX=FOLFOX4 therapy has a protective effect with respect to Sinusiodal Injury. Background. Due to modern imaging techniques the incidence of primary cystic neoplasms of the pancreas is increasing. During the last decades all pancreatic cysts were treated operatively. Depending on type and size a more conservative approach can be advocated. Methods. Review of the literature and presentation of institutional experience. Results. From 43 patients, 11 (33%) were discovered incidentally and 22 (77%) had symptoms at time of diagnosis. 33 (78%) underwent operative treatment, whereas 10 (22%) were treated conservatively. Malignancy was found in nine (27%) operated patients. Seven patients (78%) with malignant cystic neoplasm and 15 patients (63%) with a benign cystic neoplasm had symptoms. Median cyst size was 3.5 cm (1.5-12) . There was one case of malignancy within cystic lesion smaller than 3 cm. Conclusions. Therapy can be tailored depending on size and character of the pancreatic cyst. Surgical treatment alone is no longer pivotal. Does pT2 and pT3 subclassification in colorectal cancer facilitate outcome prediction in affected patients? Background. Assessing the extent of mesocolic=mesorectal tumour invasion (pT3 subclassification) has been proven useful for risk stratification of affected patients. To the best of our knowledge, data regarding the potential prognostic value of a pT2 subclassification are lacking. Methods. Three hundred and eight one patients with colorectal cancer operated between 1992 and 2000 were randomly selected for analysis. Patient records and histopathological slides were re-evaluated with respect to tumour stage and grade. pT2 classification was subdivided as follows: pT2a with infiltration of the inner circumferential and pT2b with infiltration of the outer longitudinal layer of the muscularis propria. pT3 classification was subdivided by measuring the maximal tumour invasion beyond the outer border of the muscularis propria: pT3a 1 mm, pT3b> 1-5 mm, pT3c > 5-15 mm and pT3d > 15 mm. Associations between tumour classification, tumour grade and nodal status were analyzed as well as progression-free survival. Results. Regarding patient outcome, no significant difference was detected between patients with pT2a or pT2b tumours. The pT3 subclassification, however, proved useful in predicting disease progression: 11=47 (23%) pT3a, 23=75 (31%) pT3b, 29=49 (59%) pT3c and 14=24 (58%) pT3d cases developed progressive disease (p < 0.001; log-rank test). These data were confirmed in multivariate analysis using the 5 mm cut-off level (pT3a=3b vs. pT3c=3d; p < 0.01). Conclusions. pT3 subclassification proved feasible in our patients, a cut-off level of 5 mm maximal tumour invasion beyond the outer border of the muscularis propria is recommended. Although the proposed pT2 subclassification tended to correlate with nodal status, no prognostic significance was observed. Background. Assessment of colorectal cancer prognosis is important for surveillance and optimal therapy. T-classification is an important prognostic parameter and represents tumour depth. Little is known about horizontal tumour extent. Aim of our study was to investigate the impact of tumour size on patient's outcome. Methods. Between 1.1.1992 and 31.12.2000 400 patients were random sampled of a total of 7564 patients with colorectal cancer in Styria. Complete data were available in 381 patients (215 females) and histology was reviewed by two pathologists. Results. The median tumour size in largest diameter was 4.5 cm (range 0.6-15 cm) and 28% had their tumour in the right, 29% in the left colon and 43% in the rectosigmoid or rectum. Tumour size was associated with tumour location, T-Status, N-Status, Differentiation and UICC-stage. Actuarial 5-year overall survival rates for patients with CRCs 4.5 cm and patients with CRCs > 4.5 cm were 65% and 47%, respectively. Furthermore, tumour size was independent associated with overall (p ¼ 0.029) and disease-free survival (p ¼ 0.034). Conclusions. Tumour size is an important prognostic parameter in patients with colorectal cancer and associated with overall and progression.-free survival. Background. Neoadjuvant chemotherapy (NAC) is equivalent to adjuvant therapy (AC). Many institutions apply additional AC after NAC and surgery based on risk factors. This extended chemotherapy (E Â C) is not evidence based. The study aim was to investigate whether E Â C resulted in better disease-free (DFS) and overall survival (OS). Methods. Between 1998 and 2006 369 patients received either NAC (43 pts), AC (233 pts) or E Â C (93 pts). NAC consisted in 93% of 3-6 Â epirubicin þ docetaxel(ED), in a few cases epirubicin þ cyclophosphamide (EC) AE fluorouracil or single agents. AC consisted of cmF in the beginning and EC AE taxanes in $70%. Median follow-up was 30.57 and 55 months. Hormone therapy was given in 66%, radiation therapy in 78% and breast conserving therapy was possible in 58%. Results. UICC-stages (0-III) were 4,22,53 and 21%. After NAC (135 patients), downstaging was achieved in 35% and pCR in 10%. E Â C resulted in significant reduction of DFS: compared to 85 and 83% in the NAC-and AC-groups, actuarial DFS was 63% in the E Â C-group (p < 0.01). Local=regional and distant recurrences were also significantly higher in the E Â C-group (p ¼ 0.03 and p < 0.01), whereas OS wasn't significantly affected after Cox regression. Conclusions. E Â C didn't show benefits for DFS and OS concordant with NSABP B-27-results, where additional 4Â taxane to 4Â doxorubicin þ cyclophosphamide did not improve DFS and OS. Contrariwise, we found reduced DFS and higher local=regional and distant recurrence rates and we could not identify subgroups that profited from E Â C. No differences were found between NAC-and AC-groups as in numerous studies before. Unless randomized-controlled-trials show advantages, use of extended chemotherapy after neoadjuvant therapy should be considered very carefully. Effect of preoperative radiochemotherapy on lymph node retrieval in resection of rectal cancer Background. Detection of lymph node metastases provides important prognostic information and facilitates decision-making with regards to adjuvant therapy. It has been suggested that patients in whom a small number of nodes are present in the excised specimen have a worse prognosis, due to inadequate lymphadenectomy and consequent understaging of the disease. Impact of neoadjuvant therapy on lymph node yield is not well understood. We analysed the impact of neoadjuvant therapy on tumor regression and lymph node harvest. Methods. In the period from 2004 to 2006 130 patients (63%) underwent surgery without receiving preoperative radiochemotherapy. 77 patients (37%) received long course of preoperative radiochemotherapy (50 Gy), with delayed surgery. They all underwent conventional open low anterior or abdominoperineal resection of the rectum. Results. The number of lymph nodes identified within the excised specimen in patients undergoing resection positively correlates with the pT stage as well as size of the tumour and is also dependent on the examining histopathologist. Average number of lymph nodes was lower after neoadjuvant therapy (16.4 vs. 13.7). It was also lower in every single pT group after neoadjuvant therapy. Among 6 patients with complete tumor response (pT0) there were 2 Nþ cases. In node-positive patients the number of involved nodes increases with increasing lymph node yield. Conclusions. Although neoadjuvant therapy down-stages and down-sizes rectal cancer, it results in a significantly low yield of lymph nodes, which are smaller than those in nonirradiated controls. Involved lymph nodes can be present also after complete tumor response (pT0). The risk of secondary malignancies in patients with itraductal papillary mucinous neoplasm of the pancreas Background. Due to modern imaging techniques the incidence of primary cystic neoplasms of the pancreas is increasing. These include intraductal papillary mucinous neoplasm (IPMN), which could be adenomatous to carcinomatous. There are reports that IPMNs are associated with a higher incidence of other malignancies. Methods. To report our single institutional experience and review literature. Results. During 1998 and 2006, 14 patients were diagnosed with IPMN of the pancreas. 8 (57%) female and 6 (43%) male patients have been treated and the mean age was 64 years, ranging from 49 to 82 at the time of operation. IPMN-carcinoma was found in 8 patients, while IPMN-adenoma was seen in 4 and borderline leason in 2 patients. Ten patients had history of pancreatities. Upper abdominal pain was the leading symptom in 7 patients, one had jaundice and 6 IPMNs were diagnosed incidentally. Five patients reported positive cancer-history of first degree relatives. Other malignancies occurred in five patients (36%), including breast cancer, melanoma, lyomyosarcoma, M. Hodgkin and squamous cell carcinoma. Pylorus preserving duodenopancreatectomy was performed in most cases. Postoperative mortality was 0%; one patient underwent re-operation because of intra-abdominal abscess and there was one case of pancreatic fistula. Median follow up was 31 month, 3 patients with IPMN-carcinoma, but without secondary malignancy, died due to tumor recurrence after 14, 27 and 32 months. Secondary malignancy was neither related to age, sex nor site of the tumor. Conclusions. IPMN is related with high incidence of other malignancies as reported in other larger series. Neue Lasertechnologie in der resezierenden Leberchirurgie. Erste Ergebnisse einer Phase-I-Studie Background. So far, no detailed analysis of the prognostic significance of differentiating non-functioning neuroendocrine pancreatic carcinomas (PC) has been presented. Therefore we evaluated the influence of distinguishing between well and poorly differentiated nonfunctioning neuroendocrine PC. Methods. Six well differentiated and 11 poorly differentiated nonfunctioning neuroendocrine PC were retrospectively analyzed for differences and compared with 340 ductal PC. Results. There was no dependence of pT categories on well or poorly differentiated nonfunctioning neuroendocrine PC or on ductal PC. The rate of the pN1 category was with 20% lower in well differentiated lesions than in poorly differentiated lesions (66%) and in the ductal PC group (75%) -p ¼ 0.019. In terms of R0 resections analysis showed that well differentiated lesions fared significantly better than ductal PC (p ¼ 0.014). no difference was detected between poorly differentiated ledions and ductal carcinomas (p ¼ 0.884). The outcome following R1=R2 resections for poorly differentiated neuroendocrine PC tended to be similar than for ductal PC (1-year survival rate 20% vs. 33%). Also no benefit in survival was found between poorly differentiated nonfunctioning neuroendocrine and ductal PC subjected to palliative procedures (9 months). Conclusions. For poorly differentiated nonfunctioning neuroendocrine PC the outcome was as poor as for ductal PC. The better outcome of surgical treatment of nonfunctioning neuroendocrine PC vs. that of ductal PC was determinated to well differentiated neuroendocrine lesions. These results underscore the importance to make precise distinction between well and poorly differentiated nonfunctioning neuroendocrine PC. Liverpacking and navigated RFA to treat ''inoperable'' malignant liver tumors Background. This study describes the first experience using optimized computer-assisted RFA as lastline therapy in patients with multi-focal liver malignancies unsuitable for surgical resection or standard RFA. Methods. Non-resectable liver tumors in 25 patients had to be isolated from adjacent organs by laparoscopic liver mobilization and packing (05=2004-11=2007). Bile duct cooling was accomplished in one patient. Navigated RFA comprised body fixation, contrast-enhanced CT, 3D planning, navigation, targeting and needle placement in apnea, image fusion, thermal ablation and intervention CT for quality control. Liver packing was subsequently removed laparoscopically. Results. One hundred and two visible tumors (48 primary tumors, 52 metastases) of the liver (tumor size: 1.0-11.0 cm) were successfully ablated after laparoscopic liverpacking by CT-guided frameless stereotactic RFA (9-18 RF needles=patient simultaneously). Liverpacking effectively prevented thermal injury in all patients. Early complications were observed in 4 (1 bleeding, 1 duodenal lesion due to adhesiolyis, 2 portal vein thrombosis) and late complications in 5 patients (3 infections, 2 bilioma), respectively. 30-day mortality yielded 0.04%. A CT scan after four weeks revealed total necrosis in 100% of treated tumors. Ten patients developed recurrence of their disease within a followup of 17 months allowing repeated ablation therapy in 4 of them. Conclusions. For the first time an effective multi-modal (allin-one) treatment including laparoscopic liverpacking, bile duct cooling and high-tech RFA is described as a lastline therapy for patients with liver malignancies unsuitable for surgical resection or standard RFA. Primary or recurrent ovarian cancer with diffuse peritoneal carcinomatosissubstantial improvements by an interdisciplinary multimodal approach Methods. Fifty-nine patients (pats), mean age of 56 years, who have primary or recurrent ovarian cancer with diffuse PC were treated by cytoreductive surgery and IHCP till 7=2006. Twelve pats had no prior therapy, 19 were pre-treated heavily. Twenty four pats underwent extensive prior surgery. Results. Cytoreduction to residual tumor size (RTS) < 10 mm was achieved in 33 pats. Secondary peritonectomy procedure (n ¼ 24) was successful (residual tumor size < 10 mm) in 10 pts. Two pats died within 30 days due to MOF (no deaths after 2000) . Severe post therapeutic complications (n ¼ 10 pts) are: intestinal fistulas =3, intraabdominal abscess=2, intraabdominal haemorrhage=2, renal failure=2, pulmonary embolism.=1. Analysis confirmed the extent of pre-treatment and RTS as important prognostic factors. Mean overall survival for an optimal selected subgroup of 24 pats (none or only 1 prior treatment, RTS < 10 mm) is 54.6 months, in contrast to the remaining pats with an OS of 20.1 months. Conclusions. Peritonectomy plus IHCP and systemic ChTÂ enable prolonged OS in pats with peritoneally advanced ovarian cancer. Multifocal gastrointestinal stroma tumors (GIST) with lymph node metastasescase report and an overview of literature Background. GISTs are rare mesenchymal tumors of the gastrointestinal tract. Localisation sites are stomach (60%), small intestine (30%), duodenum (5%)colorectum (5%) and other abdominal organs ( < 1%). The most common presentation of GIST is gastrointestinal bleeding. GISTs usually occur in older adults, in younger patients they are rare and not well characterized. A 26-year-old patient with multifocal GIST and multiple lymphnode involvement is presented. Patient history and therapy. The patient was admitted with recurrent gastrointestinal bleeding. Gastroscopy was performed and samples taken for histological examination. Preoperative assessment (endosonography, capsule endoscopy, CT and PET scan) was highly suspicious of multifocal GIST. Gastrectomy with radical lymphnode dissection was performed. Histological examination showed a multifocal gastrointestinal stroma tumor with multiple lymph node metastasis (12=49). The patient refused adjuvant systemic therapy (imatinib). Genetic evaluation. Histological material was sent to molec-ular=genetic analysis for c-kit and pdgfr . Concerning c-kit, no mutation or polymorphism could be found, but pdgfr showed in exon 18 a somatic silent mutation on nucleotid position 125. Conclusions. Against the common opinion GIST can be multifocal and is predominately found in young females and children. Lymphnode metastasis are very rare, still the overall prognosis is favourable. Due to the very limited experience with this special GIST type, there is yet no clear recommondation for adjuvant therapy. Background. Hepatocellular carcinoma (HCC) that meets the Milan criteria is a common indication for orthotopic liver transplantation (OLT). Recurrence-free 1-year survival has been reprted beyond 84,7%, 5-year survival beyond 61.8% [Onaca et al.: Liver Transpl. 2007 Feb 22; 13(3) :391-399]. The occurence of esophageal metastases after OLT due to HCC has not been reported in the literature. Methods. We report the case of a 55-year-old patient who underwent OLT because of hepatocellular carcinoma. The diagnosis of HCC was 7 months before OLT. Pre-operative downstaging was performed by chemoembolisation (lipiodol=famorubicin) at 5.5 and 1.5 months prior to OLT. Two lesions (1.5 cm, segment II, and 1.5 cm, segment I) could be sufficiently embolized, one lesion with 1.5 cm diameter in the right lobe could not be embolized. Pre-transplant staging showed no extrahepatic HCC metastases. Results. OLT was without complications. Immunosuppression consisted of Sirolimus (Sir) monotherapy. 8 months after OLT a gastroscopy was performed because of dysphagia. Several lesions in the distal esophagus were detected, which were verified histiologically as esophageal metastases of the HCC. Local therapy consisted of hyperthermia, photodynamic therapy and stent implantation in the distal esophagus. Nine months after OLT multiple recurrent metastatic lesions of the HCC were detected in the liver by computed tomography. The patient died 17 months after OLT due to HCC recurrence. Conclusions. Esophageal metastases of HCC are a possible complication after OLT for HCC. Only local therapeutic strategies are available. Failure of intraoperative margin assessment in breast conserving therapy of invasive breast carcinoma seems to be influenced by associated DCIS ing therapy (BCT) of invasive breast carcinoma (IBC) and to find causes for failure. Methods. One hundred and sixty eight specimens from 163 patients (age 33-89 years; median 60) with IBC treated by segmental resection were analyzed retrospectively (including 37 specimens from 34 patients with neoadjuvant chemotherapy). Intraoperative assessment included gross examination of the sliced specimen and FS of 1-2 tissue blocks from the closest distance to the margin. This distance was reassessed in permanent sections (PS). The margin status was categorized as involved (R-1), close ( < 1 mm), free (! 1 mm) and equivocal (R-x). Results. The margins were involved in 12.5% and close in 14.3%, respectively. Immediate re-excision led to free margins in all but 4% of the cases. Including PS intraoperative margin analysis failed in 19%. IBC with a DCIS component failed more often (41.1%) compared to IBC without DCIS (8.7%) (p < 0.001; 2 -test). Failure of intraoperative tumor detection was caused by IBC 5 mm and preoperative chemotherapy and also associated with failure of intraoperative margin analysis (p ¼ 0.0001). Lobular histology and preoperative chemotherapy were not significant for failure of free margins. Subsequent re-excision or mastectomy showed residual DCIS in 35% and IBC in 27%. Conclusions. Intraoperative FS of IBC margins may prevent additional surgery but may fail due to associated DCIS. A modified surgical strategy for cases with preoperatively diagnosed associated DCIS needs to be developed to prevent additional operations.
